BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tVI.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF INTRODUCES HIMSELF AT THE PALACE.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The highway glistened with many-hued pebble,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A by-path led the liegemen together.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [1]Firm and hand-locked the war-burnie glistened,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ring-sword radiant rang 'mid the armor
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 As the party was approaching the palace together
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They set their arms and armor against the wall.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In warlike equipments. 'Gainst the wall of the building
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their wide-fashioned war-shields they weary did set then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[13]      Battle-shields sturdy; benchward they turned then;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their battle-sarks rattled, the gear of the heroes;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 The lances stood up then, all in a cluster,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The arms of the seamen, ashen-shafts mounted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With edges of iron: the armor-clad troopers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A Danish hero asks them whence and why they are come.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were decked with weapons. Then a proud-mooded hero
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Asked of the champions questions of lineage:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 "From what borders bear ye your battle-shields plated,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gilded and gleaming, your gray-colored burnies,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Helmets with visors and heap of war-lances?--
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Hrothgar the king I am servant and liegeman.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mong folk from far-lands found I have never
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He expresses no little admiration for the strangers.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Men so many of mien more courageous.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I ween that from valor, nowise as outlaws,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But from greatness of soul ye sought for King Hrothgar."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf replies.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the strength-famous earlman answer rendered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The proud-mooded Wederchief replied to his question,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{We are Higelac's table-companions, and bear an important commission to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tyour prince.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Hardy 'neath helmet: "Higelac's mates are we;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf hight I. To the bairn of Healfdene,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The famous folk-leader, I freely will tell
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To thy prince my commission, if pleasantly hearing
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He'll grant we may greet him so gracious to all men."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Wulfgar replied then (he was prince of the Wendels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His boldness of spirit was known unto many,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His prowess and prudence): "The prince of the Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wulfgar, the thane, says that he will go and ask Hrothgar whether he will
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tsee the strangers.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The friend-lord of Danemen, I will ask of thy journey,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The giver of rings, as thou urgest me do it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 The folk-chief famous, and inform thee early
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What answer the good one mindeth to render me."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He turned then hurriedly where Hrothgar was sitting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [2]Old and hoary, his earlmen attending him;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The strength-famous went till he stood at the shoulder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Of the lord of the Danemen, of courteous thanemen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The custom he minded. Wulfgar addressed then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His friendly liegelord: "Folk of the Geatmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[14]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He thereupon urges his liegelord to receive the visitors courteously.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the way of the waters are wafted hither,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faring from far-lands: the foremost in rank
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 The battle-champions Beowulf title.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They make this petition: with thee, O my chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To be granted a conference; O gracious King Hrothgar,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Friendly answer refuse not to give them!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar, too, is struck with Beowulf's appearance.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In war-trappings weeded worthy they seem
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Of earls to be honored; sure the atheling is doughty
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who headed the heroes hitherward coming."

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tVII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR AND BEOWULF.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar remembers Beowulf as a youth, and also remembers his father.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar answered, helm of the Scyldings:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "I remember this man as the merest of striplings.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His father long dead now was Ecgtheow titled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Him Hrethel the Geatman granted at home his
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 One only daughter; his battle-brave son
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is come but now, sought a trustworthy friend.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seafaring sailors asserted it then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is reported to have the strength of thirty men.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who valuable gift-gems of the Geatmen[1] carried
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As peace-offering thither, that he thirty men's grapple
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Has in his hand, the hero-in-battle.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God hath sent him to our rescue.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The holy Creator usward sent him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To West-Dane warriors, I ween, for to render
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst Grendel's grimness gracious assistance:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I shall give to the good one gift-gems for courage.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Hasten to bid them hither to speed them,[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To see assembled this circle of kinsmen;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tell them expressly they're welcome in sooth to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The men of the Danes." To the door of the building
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[15]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wulfgar invites the strangers in.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wulfgar went then, this word-message shouted:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 "My victorious liegelord bade me to tell you,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The East-Danes' atheling, that your origin knows he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And o'er wave-billows wafted ye welcome are hither,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Valiant of spirit. Ye straightway may enter
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Clad in corslets, cased in your helmets,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 To see King Hrothgar. Here let your battle-boards,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wood-spears and war-shafts, await your conferring."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mighty one rose then, with many a liegeman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An excellent thane-group; some there did await them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And as bid of the brave one the battle-gear guarded.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Together they hied them, while the hero did guide them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath Heorot's roof; the high-minded went then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sturdy 'neath helmet till he stood in the building.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake (his burnie did glisten,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His armor seamed over by the art of the craftsman):
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf salutes Hrothgar, and then proceeds to boast of his youthful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tachievements.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 "Hail thou, Hrothgar! I am Higelac's kinsman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And vassal forsooth; many a wonder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I dared as a stripling. The doings of Grendel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In far-off fatherland I fully did know of:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sea-farers tell us, this hall-building standeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Excellent edifice, empty and useless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To all the earlmen after evenlight's glimmer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath heaven's bright hues hath hidden its glory.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          This my earls then urged me, the most excellent of them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carles very clever, to come and assist thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Folk-leader Hrothgar; fully they knew of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His fight with the nickers.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The strength of my body. Themselves they beheld me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When I came from the contest, when covered with gore
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foes I escaped from, where five[3] I had bound,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[16]      The giant-race wasted, in the waters destroying
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 The nickers by night, bore numberless sorrows,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Weders avenged (woes had they suffered)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Enemies ravaged; alone now with Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He intends to fight Grendel unaided.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I shall manage the matter, with the monster of evil,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The giant, decide it. Thee I would therefore
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Beg of thy bounty, Bright-Danish chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lord of the Scyldings, this single petition:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not to refuse me, defender of warriors,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Friend-lord of folks, so far have I sought thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That _I_ may unaided, my earlmen assisting me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 This brave-mooded war-band, purify Heorot.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I have heard on inquiry, the horrible creature
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Since the monster uses no weapons,}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From veriest rashness recks not for weapons;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I this do scorn then, so be Higelac gracious,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My liegelord belovèd, lenient of spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 To bear a blade or a broad-fashioned target,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A shield to the onset; only with hand-grip
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I, too, shall disdain to use any.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The foe I must grapple, fight for my life then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foeman with foeman; he fain must rely on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The doom of the Lord whom death layeth hold of.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Should he crush me, he will eat my companions as he has eaten thy
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthanes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 I ween he will wish, if he win in the struggle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To eat in the war-hall earls of the Geat-folk,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boldly to swallow[4] them, as of yore he did often
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The best of the Hrethmen! Thou needest not trouble
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A head-watch to give me;[5] he will have me dripping
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[17]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{In case of my defeat, thou wilt not have the trouble of burying me.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 And dreary with gore, if death overtake me,[6]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Will bear me off bleeding, biting and mouthing me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hermit will eat me, heedless of pity,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Marking the moor-fens; no more wilt thou need then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Should I fall, send my armor to my lord, King Higelac.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Find me my food.[7] If I fall in the battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Send to Higelac the armor that serveth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To shield my bosom, the best of equipments,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Richest of ring-mails; 'tis the relic of Hrethla,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Weird is supreme}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The work of Wayland. Goes Weird as she must go!"

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    emended to 'Géatum.' If this be accepted, change '_of_ the Geatmen' to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    '_to_ the Geatmen.'

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] If t.B.'s emendation of vv. 386, 387 be accepted, the two lines,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'Hasten ... kinsmen' will read: _Hasten thou, bid the throng of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    kinsmen go into the hall together_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 420 (_b_) and 421 (_a_), B. suggests: Þær ic (on) fífelgeban
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    ýðde eotena cyn = _where I in the ocean destroyed the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    eoten-race_.--t.B. accepts B.'s "brilliant" 'fífelgeban,' omits 'on,'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    emends 'cyn' to 'hám,' arranging: Þær ic fífelgeban ýðde, eotena hám =
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _where I desolated the ocean, the home of the eotens_.--This would be
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    better but for changing 'cyn' to 'hám.'--I suggest: Þær ic fífelgeband
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (cf. nhd. Bande) ýðde, eotena cyn = _where I conquered the monster
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    band, the race of the eotens_. This makes no change except to read
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    '_fífel_' for '_fífe_.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] 'Unforhte' (444) is much disputed.--H.-So. wavers between adj. and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    adv. Gr. and B. take it as an adv. modifying _etan: Will eat the Geats
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fearlessly_.--Kl. considers this reading absurd, and proposes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'anforhte' = timid.--Understanding 'unforhte' as an adj. has this
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    advantage, viz. that it gives a parallel to 'Geátena leóde': but to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    take it as an adv. is more natural. Furthermore, to call the Geats
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'brave' might, at this point, seem like an implied thrust at the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Danes, so long helpless; while to call his own men 'timid' would be
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    befouling his own nest.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] For 'head-watch,' cf. H.-So. notes and cf. v. 2910.--Th.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translates: _Thou wilt not need my head to hide_ (i.e., thou wilt have
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    no occasion to bury me, as Grendel will devour me whole).--Simrock
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    imagines a kind of dead-watch.--Dr. H. Wood suggests: _Thou wilt not
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    have to bury so much as my head_ (for Grendel will be a thorough
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    undertaker),--grim humor.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] S. proposes a colon after 'nimeð' (l. 447). This would make no
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    essential change in the translation.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [7] Owing to the vagueness of 'feorme' (451), this passage is
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    variously translated. In our translation, H.-So.'s glossary has been
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    quite closely followed. This agrees substantially with B.'s
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translation (P. and B. XII. 87). R. translates: _Thou needst not take
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    care longer as to the consumption of my dead body._ 'Líc' is also a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    crux here, as it may mean living body or dead body.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tVIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR AND BEOWULF.--_Continued_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar responds.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar discoursed, helm of the Scyldings:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "To defend our folk and to furnish assistance,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou soughtest us hither, good friend Beowulf.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Reminiscences of Beowulf's father, Ecgtheow.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fiercest of feuds thy father engaged in,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Heatholaf killed he in hand-to-hand conflict
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mid Wilfingish warriors; then the Wederish people
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For fear of a feud were forced to disown him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thence flying he fled to the folk of the South-Danes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[18]      The race of the Scyldings, o'er the roll of the waters;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 I had lately begun then to govern the Danemen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoard-seat of heroes held in my youth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Rich in its jewels: dead was Heregar,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My kinsman and elder had earth-joys forsaken,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Healfdene his bairn. He was better than I am!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 That feud thereafter for a fee I compounded;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the weltering waters to the Wilfings I sent
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ornaments old; oaths did he swear me.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar recounts to Beowulf the horrors of Grendel's persecutions.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          It pains me in spirit to any to tell it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What grief in Heorot Grendel hath caused me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 What horror unlooked-for, by hatred unceasing.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Waned is my war-band, wasted my hall-troop;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weird hath offcast them to the clutches of Grendel.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          God can easily hinder the scather
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From deeds so direful. Oft drunken with beer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My thanes have made many boasts, but have not executed them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 O'er the ale-vessel promised warriors in armor
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They would willingly wait on the wassailing-benches
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A grapple with Grendel, with grimmest of edges.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then this mead-hall at morning with murder was reeking,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building was bloody at breaking of daylight,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The bench-deals all flooded, dripping and bloodied,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The folk-hall was gory: I had fewer retainers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dear-beloved warriors, whom death had laid hold of.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sit down to the feast, and give us comfort.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sit at the feast now, thy intents unto heroes,[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy victor-fame show, as thy spirit doth urge thee!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A bench is made ready for Beowulf and his party.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 For the men of the Geats then together assembled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the beer-hall blithesome a bench was made ready;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There warlike in spirit they went to be seated,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Proud and exultant. A liegeman did service,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[19]      Who a beaker embellished bore with decorum,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The gleeman sings}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 And gleaming-drink poured. The gleeman sang whilom
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The heroes all rejoice together.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hearty in Heorot; there was heroes' rejoicing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A numerous war-band of Weders and Danemen.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] B. and S. reject the reading given in H.-So., and suggested by
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Grtvg. B. suggests for 457-458:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t               wáere-ryhtum Þú, wine mín Béowulf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t               and for ár-stafum úsic sóhtest.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    This means: _From the obligations of clientage, my friend Beowulf, and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    for assistance thou hast sought us_.--This gives coherence to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrothgar's opening remarks in VIII., and also introduces a new motive
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    for Beowulf's coming to Hrothgar's aid.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] _Sit now at the feast, and disclose thy purposes to the victorious
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    heroes, as thy spirit urges_.--Kl. reaches the above translation by
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    erasing the comma after 'meoto' and reading 'sige-hrèðsecgum.'--There
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    are other and bolder emendations and suggestions. Of these the boldest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    is to regard 'meoto' as a verb (imperative), and read 'on sæl': _Think
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    upon gayety, etc_.--All the renderings are unsatisfactory, the one
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    given in our translation involving a zeugma.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tIX.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tUNFERTH TAUNTS BEOWULF.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unferth, a thane of Hrothgar, is jealous of Beowulf, and undertakes to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\ttwit him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Unferth spoke up, Ecglaf his son,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who sat at the feet of the lord of the Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Opened the jousting (the journey[1] of Beowulf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sea-farer doughty, gave sorrow to Unferth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 And greatest chagrin, too, for granted he never
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That any man else on earth should attain to,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gain under heaven, more glory than he):
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Did you take part in a swimming-match with Breca?}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Art thou that Beowulf with Breca did struggle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the wide sea-currents at swimming contended,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Where to humor your pride the ocean ye tried,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{'Twas mere folly that actuated you both to risk your lives on the ocean.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From vainest vaunting adventured your bodies
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In care of the waters? And no one was able
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor lief nor loth one, in the least to dissuade you
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Your difficult voyage; then ye ventured a-swimming,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Where your arms outstretching the streams ye did cover,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mere-ways measured, mixing and stirring them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glided the ocean; angry the waves were,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With the weltering of winter. In the water's possession,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ye toiled for a seven-night; he at swimming outdid thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 In strength excelled thee. Then early at morning
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the Heathoremes' shore the holm-currents tossed him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sought he thenceward the home of his fathers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beloved of his liegemen, the land of the Brondings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The peace-castle pleasant, where a people he wielded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[20]   25 Had borough and jewels. The pledge that he made thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Breca outdid you entirely.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of Beanstan hath soothly accomplished.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I ween thou wilt find thee less fortunate issue,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Much more will Grendel outdo you, if you vie with him in prowess.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though ever triumphant in onset of battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A grim grappling, if Grendel thou darest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 For the space of a night near-by to wait for!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf retaliates.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, offspring of Ecgtheow:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "My good friend Unferth, sure freely and wildly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{O friend Unferth, you are fuddled with beer, and cannot talk coherently.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou fuddled with beer of Breca hast spoken,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hast told of his journey! A fact I allege it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 That greater strength in the waters I had then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ills in the ocean, than any man else had.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We made agreement as the merest of striplings
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Promised each other (both of us then were
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{We simply kept an engagement made in early life.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Younkers in years) that we yet would adventure
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Out on the ocean; it all we accomplished.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While swimming the sea-floods, sword-blade unscabbarded
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boldly we brandished, our bodies expected
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To shield from the sharks. He sure was unable
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He _could_ not excel me, and I _would_ not excel him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To swim on the waters further than I could,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 More swift on the waves, nor _would_ I from him go.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then we two companions stayed in the ocean
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{After five days the currents separated us.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Five nights together, till the currents did part us,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weltering waters, weathers the bleakest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And nethermost night, and the north-wind whistled
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Fierce in our faces; fell were the billows.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mere fishes' mood was mightily ruffled:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And there against foemen my firm-knotted corslet,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-jointed, hardy, help did afford me;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My battle-sark braided, brilliantly gilded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A horrible sea-beast attacked me, but I slew him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Lay on my bosom. To the bottom then dragged me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A hateful fiend-scather, seized me and held me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grim in his grapple: 'twas granted me, nathless,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To pierce the monster with the point of my weapon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My obedient blade; battle offcarried
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The mighty mere-creature by means of my hand-blow.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    means 'arrival.' If so, translate the bracket: _(the arrival of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Beowulf, the brave seafarer, was a source of great chagrin to Unferth,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF SILENCES UNFERTH.--GLEE IS HIGH.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "So ill-meaning enemies often did cause me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sorrow the sorest. I served them, in quittance,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My dear sword always served me faithfully.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of surrounding the banquet deep in the ocean;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But wounded with edges early at morning

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 No longer thereafter were hindered from sailing

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That well I could see the nesses projecting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Fortune helps the brave earl.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blustering crags. Weird often saveth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 The undoomed hero if doughty his valor!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But me did it fortune[1] to fell with my weapon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nine of the nickers. Of night-struggle harder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath dome of the heaven heard I but rarely,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor of wight more woful in the waves of the ocean;

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weary from travel. Then the waters bare me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the land of the Finns, the flood with the current,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I have never heard of your doing any such bold deeds.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weltering waves. Not a word hath been told me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of deeds so daring done by thee, Unferth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 And of sword-terror none; never hath Breca
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At the play of the battle, nor either of you two,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Feat so fearless performèd with weapons
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glinting and gleaming . . . . . . . . . . . .

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{You are a slayer of brothers, and will suffer damnation, wise as you may
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tbe.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Though with cold-blooded cruelty thou killedst thy brothers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy nearest of kin; thou needs must in hell get
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Direful damnation, though doughty thy wisdom.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I tell thee in earnest, offspring of Ecglaf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Never had Grendel such numberless horrors,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 The direful demon, done to thy liegelord,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Harrying in Heorot, if thy heart were as sturdy,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Had your acts been as brave as your words, Grendel had not ravaged your
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tland so long.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy mood as ferocious as thou dost describe them.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He hath found out fully that the fierce-burning hatred,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The edge-battle eager, of all of your kindred,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Of the Victory-Scyldings, need little dismay him:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oaths he exacteth, not any he spares
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The monster is not afraid of the Danes,}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar's spirits are revived.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t      100 Take thou in charge now the noblest of houses;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Be mindful of honor, exhibiting prowess,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Watch 'gainst the foeman! Thou shalt want no enjoyments,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Survive thou safely adventure so glorious!"

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God has provided a watch for the hall.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is self-confident}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His warlike strength and the Wielder's protection.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{We will fight with nature's weapons only.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] Gr. understood 'gódra' as meaning 'advantages in battle.' This
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    rendering H.-So. rejects. The latter takes the passage as meaning that
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Grendel, though mighty and formidable, has no skill in the art of war.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] B. in his masterly articles on Beowulf (P. and B. XII.) rejects
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the division usually made at this point, 'Þá.' (711), usually rendered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'then,' he translates 'when,' and connects its clause with the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    foregoing sentence. These changes he makes to reduce the number of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'cóm's' as principal verbs. (Cf. 703, 711, 721.) With all deference to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    this acute scholar, I must say that it seems to me that the poet is
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    exhausting his resources to bring out clearly the supreme event on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    which the whole subsequent action turns. First, he (Grendel) came _in
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the wan night_; second, he came _from the moor_; third, he came _to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the hall_. Time, place from which, place to which, are all given.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tGRENDEL AND BEOWULF.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wine-joyous building, brilliant with plating,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-hall of earthmen. Not the earliest occasion
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{This was not his first visit there.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He the home and manor of Hrothgar had sought:

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Hardier hero, hall-thanes[1] more sturdy!

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The foeman trod the shining hall-pavement,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tfrom suspense.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The prospect of plenty. Providence willed not
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To permit him any more of men under heaven
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To eat in the night-time. Higelac's kinsman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Great sorrow endured how the dire-mooded creature
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[27]      In unlooked-for assaults were likely to bear him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 No thought had the monster of deferring the matter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel immediately seizes a sleeping warrior, and devours him.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A soldier asleep, suddenly tore him,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swallowed in mouthfuls: he soon had the dead man's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Feet and hands, too, eaten entirely.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nearer he strode then, the stout-hearted warrior

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf and Grendel grapple.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Snatched as he slumbered, seizing with hand-grip,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tGRENDEL IS VANQUISHED.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf has no idea of letting Grendel live.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For no cause whatever would the earlmen's defender
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Leave in life-joys the loathsome newcomer,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He deemed his existence utterly useless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To men under heaven. Many a noble
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Of Beowulf brandished his battle-sword old,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Would guard the life of his lord and protector,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The far-famous chieftain, if able to do so;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While waging the warfare, this wist they but little,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Brave battle-thanes, while his body intending
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{No weapon would harm Grendel; he bore a charmed life.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 To slit into slivers, and seeking his spirit:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the relentless foeman nor finest of weapons
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of all on the earth, nor any of war-bills
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[29]      Was willing to injure; but weapons of victory
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swords and suchlike he had sworn to dispense with.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 His death at that time must prove to be wretched,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the far-away spirit widely should journey
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Into enemies' power. This plainly he saw then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who with mirth[1] of mood malice no little
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had wrought in the past on the race of the earthmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 (To God he was hostile), that his body would fail him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But Higelac's hardy henchman and kinsman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Held him by the hand; hateful to other
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel is sorely wounded.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was each one if living. A body-wound suffered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The direful demon, damage incurable
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His body bursts.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Was seen on his shoulder, his sinews were shivered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His body did burst. To Beowulf was given
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glory in battle; Grendel from thenceward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Must flee and hide him in the fen-cliffs and marshes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sick unto death, his dwelling must look for
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Unwinsome and woful; he wist the more fully
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The monster flees away to hide in the moors.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The end of his earthly existence was nearing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His life-days' limits. At last for the Danemen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the slaughter was over, their wish was accomplished.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The comer-from-far-land had cleansed then of evil,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Wise and valiant, the war-hall of Hrothgar,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Saved it from violence. He joyed in the night-work,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In repute for prowess; the prince of the Geatmen

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bettered their burdensome bale-sorrows fully,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The craft-begot evil they erstwhile had suffered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And were forced to endure from crushing oppression,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their manifold misery. 'Twas a manifest token,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Of Grendel together) 'neath great-stretching hall-roof.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXIV.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tREJOICING OF THE DANES.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{At early dawn, warriors from far and near come together to hear of the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tnight's adventures.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the mist of the morning many a warrior
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Stood round the gift-hall, as the story is told me:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Folk-princes fared then from far and from near
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Through long-stretching journeys to look at the wonder,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 The footprints of the foeman. Few of the warriors
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Few warriors lamented Grendel's destruction.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who gazed on the foot-tracks of the inglorious creature
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His parting from life pained very deeply,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How, weary in spirit, off from those regions
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In combats conquered he carried his traces,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Fated and flying, to the flood of the nickers.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's blood dyes the waters.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There in bloody billows bubbled the currents,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The angry eddy was everywhere mingled
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And seething with gore, welling with sword-blood;[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He death-doomed had hid him, when reaved of his joyance
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 He laid down his life in the lair he had fled to,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His heathenish spirit, where hell did receive him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thence the friends from of old backward turned them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And many a younker from merry adventure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Striding their stallions, stout from the seaward,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Heroes on horses. There were heard very often
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is the hero of the hour.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf's praises; many often asserted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That neither south nor north, in the circuit of waters,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He is regarded as a probable successor to Hrothgar.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er outstretching earth-plain, none other was better
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mid bearers of war-shields, more worthy to govern,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 'Neath the arch of the ether. Not any, however,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst the friend-lord muttered, mocking-words uttered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{But no word is uttered to derogate from the old king}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of Hrothgar the gracious (a good king he).
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oft the famed ones permitted their fallow-skinned horses
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[31]      To run in rivalry, racing and chasing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Where the fieldways appeared to them fair and inviting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Known for their excellence; oft a thane of the folk-lord,[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The gleeman sings the deeds of heroes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [3]A man of celebrity, mindful of rhythms,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who ancient traditions treasured in memory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          New word-groups found properly bound:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 The bard after 'gan then Beowulf's venture
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He sings in alliterative measures of Beowulf's prowess.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wisely to tell of, and words that were clever
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To utter skilfully, earnestly speaking,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Everything told he that he heard as to Sigmund's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Also of Sigemund, who has slain a great fire-dragon.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mighty achievements, many things hidden,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The strife of the Wælsing, the wide-going ventures
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The children of men knew of but little,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The feud and the fury, but Fitela with him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When suchlike matters he minded to speak of,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Uncle to nephew, as in every contention
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Each to other was ever devoted:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A numerous host of the race of the scathers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They had slain with the sword-edge. To Sigmund accrued then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No little of glory, when his life-days were over,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since he sturdy in struggle had destroyed the great dragon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 The hoard-treasure's keeper; 'neath the hoar-grayish stone he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of the atheling, unaided adventured
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The perilous project; not present was Fitela,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yet the fortune befell him of forcing his weapon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Through the marvellous dragon, that it stood in the wall,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Well-honored weapon; the worm was slaughtered.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The great one had gained then by his glorious achievement
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To reap from the ring-hoard richest enjoyment,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[32]      As best it did please him: his vessel he loaded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shining ornaments on the ship's bosom carried,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Kinsman of Wæls: the drake in heat melted.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sigemund was widely famed.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was farthest famed of fugitive pilgrims,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mid wide-scattered world-folk, for works of great prowess,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War-troopers' shelter: hence waxed he in honor.[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heremod, an unfortunate Danish king, is introduced by way of contrast.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Afterward Heremod's hero-strength failed him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 His vigor and valor. 'Mid venomous haters
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the hands of foemen he was foully delivered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offdriven early. Agony-billows
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unlike Sigemund and Beowulf, Heremod was a burden to his people.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oppressed him too long, to his people he became then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To all the athelings, an ever-great burden;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 And the daring one's journey in days of yore
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many wise men were wont to deplore,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Such as hoped he would bring them help in their sorrow,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the son of their ruler should rise into power,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Holding the headship held by his fathers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 Should govern the people, the gold-hoard and borough,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The kingdom of heroes, the realm of the Scyldings.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is an honor to his race.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He to all men became then far more beloved,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Higelac's kinsman, to kindreds and races,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To his friends much dearer; him malice assaulted.--
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The story is resumed.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Oft running and racing on roadsters they measured
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dun-colored highways. Then the light of the morning
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was hurried and hastened. Went henchmen in numbers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the beautiful building, bold ones in spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To look at the wonder; the liegelord himself then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 From his wife-bower wending, warden of treasures,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glorious trod with troopers unnumbered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Famed for his virtues, and with him the queen-wife
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measured the mead-ways, with maidens attending.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] S. emends, suggesting 'déop' for 'déog,' and removing semicolon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    after 'wéol.' The two half-lines 'welling ... hid him' would then

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXV.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR'S GRATITUDE.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar discoursed (to the hall-building went he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He stood by the pillar,[1] saw the steep-rising hall-roof
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gleaming with gold-gems, and Grendel his hand there):
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar gives thanks for the overthrow of the monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "For the sight we behold now, thanks to the Wielder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Early be offered! Much evil I bided,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Snaring from Grendel:[2] God can e'er 'complish
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wonder on wonder, Wielder of Glory!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I had given up all hope, when this brave liegeman came to our aid.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But lately I reckoned ne'er under heaven
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Comfort to gain me for any of sorrows,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 While the handsomest of houses horrid with bloodstain
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gory uptowered; grief had offfrightened[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the wise ones who weened not that ever
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The folk-troop's defences 'gainst foes they should strengthen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst sprites and monsters. Through the might of the Wielder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 A doughty retainer hath a deed now accomplished
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which erstwhile we all with our excellent wisdom
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{If his mother yet liveth, well may she thank God for this son.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Failed to perform. May affirm very truly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What woman soever in all of the nations
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gave birth to the child, if yet she surviveth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 That the long-ruling Lord was lavish to herward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the birth of the bairn. Now, Beowulf dear,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hereafter, Beowulf, thou shalt be my son.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Most excellent hero, I'll love thee in spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As bairn of my body; bear well henceforward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The relationship new. No lack shall befall thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Of earth-joys any I ever can give thee.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Full often for lesser service I've given
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[34]      Hero less hardy hoard-treasure precious,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Thou hast won immortal distinction.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To a weaker in war-strife. By works of distinction
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou hast gained for thyself now that thy glory shall flourish
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Forever and ever. The All-Ruler quite thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With good from His hand as He hitherto did thee!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf replies: I was most happy to render thee this service.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, Ecgtheow's offspring:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "That labor of glory most gladly achieved we,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The combat accomplished, unquailing we ventured
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 The enemy's grapple; I would grant it much rather
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou wert able to look at the creature in person,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faint unto falling, the foe in his trappings!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On murder-bed quickly I minded to bind him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With firm-holding fetters, that forced by my grapple
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Low he should lie in life-and-death struggle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Less his body escape; I was wholly unable,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I could not keep the monster from escaping, as God did not will that I
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tshould.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since God did not will it, to keep him from going,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not held him that firmly, hated opposer;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Too swift was the foeman. Yet safety regarding
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 He suffered his hand behind him to linger,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His arm and shoulder, to act as watcher;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He left his hand and arm behind.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No shadow of solace the woe-begone creature
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Found him there nathless: the hated destroyer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Liveth no longer, lashed for his evils,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 But sorrow hath seized him, in snare-meshes hath him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Close in its clutches, keepeth him writhing
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In baleful bonds: there banished for evil
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The man shall wait for the mighty tribunal,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God will give him his deserts.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How the God of glory shall give him his earnings."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Then the soldier kept silent, son of old Ecglaf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unferth has nothing more to say, for Beowulf's actions speak louder than
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\twords.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From boasting and bragging of battle-achievements,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since the princes beheld there the hand that depended
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath the lofty hall-timbers by the might of the nobleman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each one before him, the enemy's fingers;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Each finger-nail strong steel most resembled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The heathen one's hand-spur, the hero-in-battle's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Claw most uncanny; quoth they agreeing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[35]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{No sword will harm the monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That not any excellent edges of brave ones
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was willing to touch him, the terrible creature's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Battle-hand bloody to bear away from him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXVI.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR LAVISHES GIFTS UPON HIS DELIVERER.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heorot is adorned with hands.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then straight was ordered that Heorot inside[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With hands be embellished: a host of them gathered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of men and women, who the wassailing-building
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The guest-hall begeared. Gold-flashing sparkled
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Webs on the walls then, of wonders a many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To each of the heroes that look on such objects.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hall is defaced, however.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The beautiful building was broken to pieces
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which all within with irons was fastened,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Its hinges torn off: only the roof was
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Whole and uninjured when the horrible creature
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Outlawed for evil off had betaken him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hopeless of living. 'Tis hard to avoid it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{[A vague passage of five verses.]}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (Whoever will do it!); but he doubtless must come to[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The place awaiting, as Wyrd hath appointed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Soul-bearers, earth-dwellers, earls under heaven,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where bound on its bed his body shall slumber
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar goes to the banquet.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When feasting is finished. Full was the time then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the son of Healfdene went to the building;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[36]      The excellent atheling would eat of the banquet.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Ne'er heard I that people with hero-band larger
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bare them better tow'rds their bracelet-bestower.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The laden-with-glory stooped to the bench then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (Their kinsmen-companions in plenty were joyful,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many a cupful quaffing complaisantly),
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Doughty of spirit in the high-tow'ring palace,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar's nephew, Hrothulf, is present.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar and Hrothulf. Heorot then inside
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was filled with friendly ones; falsehood and treachery
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Folk-Scyldings now nowise did practise.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar lavishes gifts upon Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the offspring of Healfdene offered to Beowulf
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 A golden standard, as reward for the victory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A banner embossed, burnie and helmet;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many men saw then a song-famous weapon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Borne 'fore the hero. Beowulf drank of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cup in the building; that treasure-bestowing
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 He needed not blush for in battle-men's presence.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Four handsomer gifts were never presented.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ne'er heard I that many men on the ale-bench
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In friendlier fashion to their fellows presented
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Four bright jewels with gold-work embellished.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Round the roof of the helmet a head-guarder outside
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Braided with wires, with bosses was furnished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That swords-for-the-battle fight-hardened might fail
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boldly to harm him, when the hero proceeded
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar commands that eight finely caparisoned steeds be brought to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBeowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forth against foemen. The defender of earls then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Commanded that eight steeds with bridles
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Gold-plated, gleaming, be guided to hallward,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Inside the building; on one of them stood then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An art-broidered saddle embellished with jewels;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas the sovereign's seat, when the son of King Healfdene
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was pleased to take part in the play of the edges;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 The famous one's valor ne'er failed at the front when
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Slain ones were bowing. And to Beowulf granted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The prince of the Ingwins, power over both,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er war-steeds and weapons; bade him well to enjoy them.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In so manly a manner the mighty-famed chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[37]   55 Hoard-ward of heroes, with horses and jewels
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War-storms requited, that none e'er condemneth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who willeth to tell truth with full justice.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] Kl. suggests 'hroden' for 'háten,' and renders: _Then quickly was
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Heorot adorned within, with hands bedecked_.--B. suggests 'gefrætwon'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    instead of 'gefrætwod,' and renders: _Then was it commanded to adorn
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Heorot within quickly with hands_.--The former has the advantage of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    affording a parallel to 'gefrætwod': both have the disadvantage of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    altering the text.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] The passage 1005-1009 seems to be hopeless. One difficult point is
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    to find a subject for 'gesacan.' Some say 'he'; others supply 'each,'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _i.e., every soul-bearer ... must gain the inevitable place_. The
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    genitives in this case are partitive.--If 'he' be subj., the genitives
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    are dependent on 'gearwe' (= prepared).--The 'he' itself is disputed,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXVII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBANQUET (_continued_).--THE SCOP'S SONG OF FINN AND HNÆF.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Each of Beowulf's companions receives a costly gift.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the atheling of earlmen to each of the heroes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who the ways of the waters went with Beowulf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A costly gift-token gave on the mead-bench,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offered an heirloom, and ordered that that man
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The warrior killed by Grendel is to be paid for in gold.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 With gold should be paid for, whom Grendel had erstwhile
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wickedly slaughtered, as he more of them had done
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had far-seeing God and the mood of the hero
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fate not averted: the Father then governed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          All of the earth-dwellers, as He ever is doing;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Hence insight for all men is everywhere fittest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forethought of spirit! much he shall suffer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of lief and of loathsome who long in this present
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Useth the world in this woful existence.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There was music and merriment mingling together
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar's scop recalls events in the reign of his lord's father.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Touching Healfdene's leader; the joy-wood was fingered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measures recited, when the singer of Hrothgar
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On mead-bench should mention the merry hall-joyance
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the kinsmen of Finn, when onset surprised them:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hnæf, the Danish general, is treacherously attacked while staying at
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tFinn's castle.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "The Half-Danish hero, Hnæf of the Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 On the field of the Frisians was fated to perish.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sure Hildeburg needed not mention approving
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The faith of the Jutemen: though blameless entirely,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Queen Hildeburg is not only wife of Finn, but a kinswoman of the murdered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHnæf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When shields were shivered she was shorn of her darlings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of bairns and brothers: they bent to their fate
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 With war-spear wounded; woe was that woman.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not causeless lamented the daughter of Hoce
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The decree of the Wielder when morning-light came and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She was able 'neath heaven to behold the destruction
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[38]      Of brothers and bairns, where the brightest of earth-joys
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Finn's force is almost exterminated.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 She had hitherto had: all the henchmen of Finn
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War had offtaken, save a handful remaining,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That he nowise was able to offer resistance[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hengest succeeds Hnæf as Danish general.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the onset of Hengest in the parley of battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor the wretched remnant to rescue in war from
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 The earl of the atheling; but they offered conditions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Compact between the Frisians and the Danes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Another great building to fully make ready,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A hall and a high-seat, that half they might rule with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sons of the Jutemen, and that Folcwalda's son would
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Day after day the Danemen honor
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 When gifts were giving, and grant of his ring-store
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Hengest's earl-troop ever so freely,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of his gold-plated jewels, as he encouraged the Frisians
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Equality of gifts agreed on.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the bench of the beer-hall. On both sides they swore then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A fast-binding compact; Finn unto Hengest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 With no thought of revoking vowed then most solemnly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The woe-begone remnant well to take charge of,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His Witan advising; the agreement should no one
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By words or works weaken and shatter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By artifice ever injure its value,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Though reaved of their ruler their ring-giver's slayer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They followed as vassals, Fate so requiring:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{No one shall refer to old grudges.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then if one of the Frisians the quarrel should speak of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In tones that were taunting, terrible edges
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Should cut in requital. Accomplished the oath was,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 And treasure of gold from the hoard was uplifted.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Danish warriors are burned on a funeral-pyre.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The best of the Scylding braves was then fully
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prepared for the pile; at the pyre was seen clearly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blood-gory burnie, the boar with his gilding,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The iron-hard swine, athelings many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Fatally wounded; no few had been slaughtered.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hildeburg bade then, at the burning of Hnæf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[39]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Queen Hildeburg has her son burnt along with Hnæf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bairn of her bosom to bear to the fire,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That his body be burned and borne to the pyre.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The woe-stricken woman wept on his shoulder,[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 In measures lamented; upmounted the hero.[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The greatest of dead-fires curled to the welkin,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the hill's-front crackled; heads were a-melting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wound-doors bursting, while the blood was a-coursing
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From body-bite fierce. The fire devoured them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Greediest of spirits, whom war had offcarried
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From both of the peoples; their bravest were fallen.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 1084, R. suggests 'wiht Hengeste wið gefeohtan.'--K. suggests
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'wið Hengeste wiht gefeohtan.' Neither emendation would make any
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    essential change in the translation.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] The separation of adjective and noun by a phrase (cf. v. 1118)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    being very unusual, some scholars have put 'earme on eaxle' with the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    foregoing lines, inserting a semicolon after 'eaxle.' In this case 'on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    eaxe' (_i.e._, on the ashes, cinders) is sometimes read, and this
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    affords a parallel to 'on bæl.' Let us hope that a satisfactory
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    rendering shall yet be reached without resorting to any tampering with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the text, such as Lichtenheld proposed: 'earme ides on eaxle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    gnornode.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 'gúð-rinc,' 'gúð-réc,' _battle-smoke_, has been suggested.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
