BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXVIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE FINN EPISODE (_continued_).--THE BANQUET CONTINUES.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The survivors go to Friesland, the home of Finn.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Then the warriors departed to go to their dwellings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Reaved of their friends, Friesland to visit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their homes and high-city. Hengest continued
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hengest remains there all winter, unable to get away.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Biding with Finn the blood-tainted winter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Wholly unsundered;[1] of fatherland thought he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though unable to drive the ring-stemmèd vessel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[40]      O'er the ways of the waters; the wave-deeps were tossing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fought with the wind; winter in ice-bonds
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Closed up the currents, till there came to the dwelling
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 A year in its course, as yet it revolveth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If season propitious one alway regardeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          World-cheering weathers. Then winter was gone,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earth's bosom was lovely; the exile would get him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He devises schemes of vengeance.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The guest from the palace; on grewsomest vengeance
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 He brooded more eager than on oversea journeys,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Whe'r onset-of-anger he were able to 'complish,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bairns of the Jutemen therein to remember.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nowise refused he the duties of liegeman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When Hun of the Frisians the battle-sword Láfing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Fairest of falchions, friendly did give him:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Its edges were famous in folk-talk of Jutland.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And savage sword-fury seized in its clutches
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bold-mooded Finn where he bode in his palace,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Guthlaf and Oslaf revenge Hnæf's slaughter.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the grewsome grapple Guthlaf and Oslaf
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Had mournfully mentioned, the mere-journey over,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For sorrows half-blamed him; the flickering spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Could not bide in his bosom. Then the building was covered[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Finn is slain.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With corpses of foemen, and Finn too was slaughtered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The king with his comrades, and the queen made a prisoner.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The jewels of Finn, and his queen are carried away by the Danes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The troops of the Scyldings bore to their vessels
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          All that the land-king had in his palace,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Such trinkets and treasures they took as, on searching,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At Finn's they could find. They ferried to Daneland
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The excellent woman on oversea journey,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The lay is concluded, and the main story is resumed.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Led her to their land-folk." The lay was concluded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gleeman's recital. Shouts again rose then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bench-glee resounded, bearers then offered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Skinkers carry round the beaker.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wine from wonder-vats. Wealhtheo advanced then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Going 'neath gold-crown, where the good ones were seated
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[41]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Queen Wealhtheow greets Hrothgar, as he sits beside Hrothulf, his
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tnephew.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Uncle and nephew; their peace was yet mutual,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          True each to the other. And Unferth the spokesman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sat at the feet of the lord of the Scyldings:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each trusted his spirit that his mood was courageous,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though at fight he had failed in faith to his kinsmen.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Said the queen of the Scyldings: "My lord and protector,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Treasure-bestower, take thou this beaker;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Joyance attend thee, gold-friend of heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Be generous to the Geats.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And greet thou the Geatmen with gracious responses!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So ought one to do. Be kind to the Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 In gifts not niggardly; anear and afar now
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Peace thou enjoyest. Report hath informed me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou'lt have for a bairn the battle-brave hero.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Now is Heorot cleansèd, ring-palace gleaming;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Have as much joy as possible in thy hall, once more purified.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Give while thou mayest many rewards,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 And bequeath to thy kinsmen kingdom and people,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On wending thy way to the Wielder's splendor.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I know good Hrothulf, that the noble young troopers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I know that Hrothulf will prove faithful if he survive thee.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He'll care for and honor, lord of the Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If earth-joys thou endest earlier than he doth;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 I reckon that recompense he'll render with kindness
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Our offspring and issue, if that all he remember,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What favors of yore, when he yet was an infant,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We awarded to him for his worship and pleasure."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then she turned by the bench where her sons were carousing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Hrethric and Hrothmund, and the heroes' offspring,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is sitting by the two royal sons.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-youth together; there the good one was sitting
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twixt the brothers twain, Beowulf Geatman.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 1130 (1) R. and Gr. suggest 'elne unflitme' as 1098 (1) reads.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The latter verse is undisputed; and, for the former, 'elne' would be
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as possible as 'ealles,' and 'unflitme' is well supported. Accepting
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'elne unflitme' for both, I would suggest '_very peaceably_' for both
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    places: (1) _Finn to Hengest very peaceably vowed with oaths_, etc.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (2) _Hengest then still the slaughter-stained winter remained there
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    with Finn very peaceably_. The two passages become thus correlatives,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the second a sequel of the first. 'Elne,' in the sense of very
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (swíðe), needs no argument; and 'unflitme' (from 'flítan') can, it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    seems to me, be more plausibly rendered 'peaceful,' 'peaceable,' than
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'contestable,' or 'conquerable.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] Some scholars have proposed 'roden'; the line would then read:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _Then the building was reddened, etc._, instead of 'covered.' The 'h'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    may have been carried over from the three alliterating 'h's.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXIX.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF RECEIVES FURTHER HONOR.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{More gifts are offered Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A beaker was borne him, and bidding to quaff it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Graciously given, and gold that was twisted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Pleasantly proffered, a pair of arm-jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[42]      Rings and corslet, of collars the greatest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 I've heard of 'neath heaven. Of heroes not any
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          More splendid from jewels have I heard 'neath the welkin,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A famous necklace is referred to, in comparison with the gems presented
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tto Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since Hama off bore the Brosingmen's necklace,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bracteates and jewels, from the bright-shining city,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Eormenric's cunning craftiness fled from,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Chose gain everlasting. Geatish Higelac,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grandson of Swerting, last had this jewel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When tramping 'neath banner the treasure he guarded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The field-spoil defended; Fate offcarried him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When for deeds of daring he endured tribulation,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Hate from the Frisians; the ornaments bare he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the cup of the currents, costly gem-treasures,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mighty folk-leader, he fell 'neath his target;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The[2] corpse of the king then came into charge of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The race of the Frankmen, the mail-shirt and collar:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Warmen less noble plundered the fallen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the fight was finished; the folk of the Geatmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The field of the dead held in possession.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The choicest of mead-halls with cheering resounded.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wealhtheo discoursed, the war-troop addressed she:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Queen Wealhtheow magnifies Beowulf's achievements.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 "This collar enjoy thou, Beowulf worthy,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Young man, in safety, and use thou this armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gems of the people, and prosper thou fully,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Show thyself sturdy and be to these liegemen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mild with instruction! I'll mind thy requital.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Thou hast brought it to pass that far and near
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forever and ever earthmen shall honor thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Even so widely as ocean surroundeth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blustering bluffs. Be, while thou livest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[43]      A wealth-blessèd atheling. I wish thee most truly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{May gifts never fail thee.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Jewels and treasure. Be kind to my son, thou
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Living in joyance! Here each of the nobles
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is true unto other, gentle in spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Loyal to leader. The liegemen are peaceful,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-troops ready: well-drunken heroes,[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Do as I bid ye." Then she went to the settle.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There was choicest of banquets, wine drank the heroes:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They little know of the sorrow in store for them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weird they knew not, destiny cruel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As to many an earlman early it happened,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When evening had come and Hrothgar had parted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Off to his manor, the mighty to slumber.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Warriors unnumbered warded the building
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As erst they did often: the ale-settle bared they,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas covered all over with beds and pillows.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A doomed thane is there with them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Doomed unto death, down to his slumber
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Bowed then a beer-thane. Their battle-shields placed they,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bright-shining targets, up by their heads then;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the atheling on ale-bench 'twas easy to see there
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Battle-high helmet, burnie of ring-mail,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They were always ready for battle.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And mighty war-spear. 'Twas the wont of that people
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 To constantly keep them equipped for the battle,[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At home or marching--in either condition--
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At seasons just such as necessity ordered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As best for their ruler; that people was worthy.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] C. suggests a semicolon after 'city,' with 'he' as supplied
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    subject of 'fled' and 'chose.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'feorh' S. suggests 'feoh': 'corpse' in the translation would
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    then be changed to '_possessions_,' '_belongings_.' This is a better
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reading than one joining, in such intimate syntactical relations,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    things so unlike as 'corpse' and 'jewels.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] S. suggests '_wine-joyous heroes_,' '_warriors elated with wine_.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] I believe this translation brings out the meaning of the poet,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    without departing seriously from the H.-So. text. 'Oft' frequently
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    means 'constantly,' 'continually,' not always 'often.'--Why 'an (on)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    wíg gearwe' should be written 'ánwíg-gearwe' (= ready for single
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    combat), I cannot see. 'Gearwe' occurs quite frequently with 'on'; cf.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    B. 1110 (_ready for the pyre_), El. 222 (_ready for the glad
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    journey_). Moreover, what has the idea of single combat to do with B.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    1247 ff.? The poet is giving an inventory of the arms and armor which
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    they lay aside on retiring, and he closes his narration by saying that
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    they were _always prepared for battle both at home and on the march_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[44]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXX.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE MOTHER OF GRENDEL.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They sank then to slumber. With sorrow one paid for
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His evening repose, as often betid them
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While Grendel was holding[1] the gold-bedecked palace,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ill-deeds performing, till his end overtook him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Death for his sins. 'Twas seen very clearly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's mother is known to be thirsting for revenge.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Known unto earth-folk, that still an avenger
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Outlived the loathed one, long since the sorrow
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Caused by the struggle; the mother of Grendel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Devil-shaped woman, her woe ever minded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Who was held to inhabit the horrible waters,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{[Grendel's progenitor, Cain, is again referred to.]}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cold-flowing currents, after Cain had become a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Slayer-with-edges to his one only brother,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of his sire; he set out then banished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Marked as a murderer, man-joys avoiding,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Lived in the desert. Thence demons unnumbered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The poet again magnifies Beowulf's valor.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fate-sent awoke; one of them Grendel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sword-cursèd, hateful, who at Heorot met with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A man that was watching, waiting the struggle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where a horrid one held him with hand-grapple sturdy;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Nathless he minded the might of his body,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The glorious gift God had allowed him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And folk-ruling Father's favor relied on,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His help and His comfort: so he conquered the foeman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hell-spirit humbled: he unhappy departed then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Reaved of his joyance, journeying to death-haunts,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foeman of man. His mother moreover
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's mother comes to avenge her son.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Eager and gloomy was anxious to go on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her mournful mission, mindful of vengeance
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the death of her son. She came then to Heorot
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[45]   30 Where the Armor-Dane earlmen all through the building
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were lying in slumber. Soon there became then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Return[2] to the nobles, when the mother of Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Entered the folk-hall; the fear was less grievous
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By even so much as the vigor of maidens,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 War-strength of women, by warrior is reckoned,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When well-carved weapon, worked with the hammer,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Blade very bloody, brave with its edges,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Strikes down the boar-sign that stands on the helmet.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the hard-edgèd weapon was heaved in the building,[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The brand o'er the benches, broad-lindens many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-fast were lifted; for helmet he recked not,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For armor-net broad, whom terror laid hold of.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She went then hastily, outward would get her
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her life for to save, when some one did spy her;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She seizes a favorite liegemen of Hrothgar's.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Soon she had grappled one of the athelings
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fast and firmly, when fenward she hied her;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That one to Hrothgar was liefest of heroes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In rank of retainer where waters encircle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A mighty shield-warrior, whom she murdered at slumber,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 A broadly-famed battle-knight. Beowulf was absent,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf was asleep in another part of the palace.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But another apartment was erstwhile devoted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the glory-decked Geatman when gold was distributed.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There was hubbub in Heorot. The hand that was famous
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She grasped in its gore;[4] grief was renewed then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[46]   55 In homes and houses: 'twas no happy arrangement
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In both of the quarters to barter and purchase
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With lives of their friends. Then the well-agèd ruler,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gray-headed war-thane, was woful in spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When his long-trusted liegeman lifeless he knew of,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is sent for.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 His dearest one gone. Quick from a room was
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf brought, brave and triumphant.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As day was dawning in the dusk of the morning,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He comes at Hrothgar's summons.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went then that earlman, champion noble,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came with comrades, where the clever one bided
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Whether God all gracious would grant him a respite
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          After the woe he had suffered. The war-worthy hero
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With a troop of retainers trod then the pavement
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (The hall-building groaned), till he greeted the wise one,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf inquires how Hrothgar had enjoyed his night's rest.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earl of the Ingwins;[5] asked if the night had
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Fully refreshed him, as fain he would have it.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] Several eminent authorities either read or emend the MS. so as to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    make this verse read, _While Grendel was wasting the gold-bedecked
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    palace_. So 20_15 below: _ravaged the desert_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'sóna' (1281), t.B. suggests 'sára,' limiting 'edhwyrft.' Read
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    then: _Return of sorrows to the nobles, etc_. This emendation supplies
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the syntactical gap after 'edhwyrft.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] Some authorities follow Grein's lexicon in treating 'heard ecg' as
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    an adj. limiting 'sweord': H.-So. renders it as a subst. (So v. 1491.)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The sense of the translation would be the same.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] B. suggests 'under hróf genam' (v. 1303). This emendation, as well
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as an emendation with (?) to v. 739, he offers, because 'under'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    baffles him in both passages. All we need is to take 'under' in its
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    secondary meaning of 'in,' which, though not given by Grein, occurs in
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the literature. Cf. Chron. 876 (March's A.-S. Gram. § 355) and Oro.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Amaz. I. 10, where 'under' = _in the midst of_. Cf. modern Eng. 'in
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    such circumstances,' which interchanges in good usage with 'under such
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    circumstances.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] For 'néod-laðu' (1321) C. suggests 'néad-láðum,' and translates:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _asked whether the night had been pleasant to him after
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    crushing-hostility_.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXI.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR'S ACCOUNT OF THE MONSTERS.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar laments the death of Æschere, his shoulder-companion.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar rejoined, helm of the Scyldings:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Ask not of joyance! Grief is renewed to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The folk of the Danemen. Dead is Æschere,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yrmenlaf's brother, older than he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 My true-hearted counsellor, trusty adviser,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shoulder-companion, when fighting in battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Our heads we protected, when troopers were clashing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He was my ideal hero.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And heroes were dashing; such an earl should be ever,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An erst-worthy atheling, as Æschere proved him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 The flickering death-spirit became in Heorot
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His hand-to-hand murderer; I can not tell whither
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cruel one turned in the carcass exulting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[47]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{This horrible creature came to avenge Grendel's death.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By cramming discovered.[1] The quarrel she wreaked then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That last night igone Grendel thou killedst
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 In grewsomest manner, with grim-holding clutches,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since too long he had lessened my liege-troop and wasted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My folk-men so foully. He fell in the battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With forfeit of life, and another has followed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A mighty crime-worker, her kinsman avenging,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 And henceforth hath 'stablished her hatred unyielding,[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As it well may appear to many a liegeman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who mourneth in spirit the treasure-bestower,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her heavy heart-sorrow; the hand is now lifeless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which[3] availed you in every wish that you cherished.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I have heard my vassals speak of these two uncanny monsters who lived in
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthe moors.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Land-people heard I, liegemen, this saying,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dwellers in halls, they had seen very often
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A pair of such mighty march-striding creatures,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far-dwelling spirits, holding the moorlands:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One of them wore, as well they might notice,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The image of woman, the other one wretched
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In guise of a man wandered in exile,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Except he was huger than any of earthmen;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earth-dwelling people entitled him Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In days of yore: they know not their father,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Whe'r ill-going spirits any were borne him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The inhabit the most desolate and horrible places.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ever before. They guard the wolf-coverts,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lands inaccessible, wind-beaten nesses,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fearfullest fen-deeps, where a flood from the mountains
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath mists of the nesses netherward rattles,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The stream under earth: not far is it henceward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measured by mile-lengths that the mere-water standeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which forests hang over, with frost-whiting covered,[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[48]      A firm-rooted forest, the floods overshadow.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There ever at night one an ill-meaning portent
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 A fire-flood may see; 'mong children of men
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          None liveth so wise that wot of the bottom;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though harassed by hounds the heath-stepper seek for,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Even the hounded deer will not seek refuge in these uncanny regions.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fly to the forest, firm-antlered he-deer,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Spurred from afar, his spirit he yieldeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 His life on the shore, ere in he will venture
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To cover his head. Uncanny the place is:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thence upward ascendeth the surging of waters,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wan to the welkin, when the wind is stirring
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weathers unpleasing, till the air groweth gloomy,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{To thee only can I look for assistance.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 And the heavens lower. Now is help to be gotten
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From thee and thee only! The abode thou know'st not,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dangerous place where thou'rt able to meet with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sin-laden hero: seek if thou darest!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the feud I will fully fee thee with money,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 With old-time treasure, as erstwhile I did thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With well-twisted jewels, if away thou shalt get thee."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'gefrægnod' (1334), K. and t.B. suggest 'gefægnod,' rendering
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    '_rejoicing in her fill_.' This gives a parallel to 'æse wlanc'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (1333).
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] The line 'And ... yielding,' B. renders: _And she has performed a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    deed of blood-vengeance whose effect is far-reaching_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] 'Sé Þe' (1345) is an instance of masc. rel. with fem. antecedent.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    So v. 1888, where 'sé Þe' refers to 'yldo.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] For 'hrímge' in the H.-So. edition, Gr. and others read 'hrínde'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (=hrínende), and translate: _which rustling forests overhang_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF SEEKS GRENDEL'S MOTHER.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, Ecgtheow's son:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf exhorts the old king to arouse himself for action.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Grieve not, O wise one! for each it is better,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His friend to avenge than with vehemence wail him;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of us must the end-day abide of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 His earthly existence; who is able accomplish
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glory ere death! To battle-thane noble
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lifeless lying, 'tis at last most fitting.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Arise, O king, quick let us hasten
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To look at the footprint of the kinsman of Grendel!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 I promise thee this now: to his place he'll escape not,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To embrace of the earth, nor to mountainous forest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor to depths of the ocean, wherever he wanders.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[49]      Practice thou now patient endurance
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of each of thy sorrows, as I hope for thee soothly!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar rouses himself. His horse is brought.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Then up sprang the old one, the All-Wielder thanked he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ruler Almighty, that the man had outspoken.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then for Hrothgar a war-horse was decked with a bridle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Curly-maned courser. The clever folk-leader
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They start on the track of the female monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Stately proceeded: stepped then an earl-troop
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Of linden-wood bearers. Her footprints were seen then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Widely in wood-paths, her way o'er the bottoms,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where she faraway fared o'er fen-country murky,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bore away breathless the best of retainers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who pondered with Hrothgar the welfare of country.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The son of the athelings then went o'er the stony,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Declivitous cliffs, the close-covered passes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Narrow passages, paths unfrequented,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nesses abrupt, nicker-haunts many;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One of a few of wise-mooded heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 He onward advanced to view the surroundings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till he found unawares woods of the mountain
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er hoar-stones hanging, holt-wood unjoyful;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The water stood under, welling and gory.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas irksome in spirit to all of the Danemen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Friends of the Scyldings, to many a liegeman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The sight of Æschere's head causes them great sorrow.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sad to be suffered, a sorrow unlittle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To each of the earlmen, when to Æschere's head they
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came on the cliff. The current was seething
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With blood and with gore (the troopers gazed on it).
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The horn anon sang the battle-song ready.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The troop were all seated; they saw 'long the water then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The water is filled with serpents and sea-dragons.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many a serpent, mere-dragons wondrous
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Trying the waters, nickers a-lying
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the cliffs of the nesses, which at noonday full often
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Go on the sea-deeps their sorrowful journey,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wild-beasts and wormkind; away then they hastened
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{One of them is killed by Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hot-mooded, hateful, they heard the great clamor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-trumpet winding. One did the Geat-prince
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[50]      Sunder from earth-joys, with arrow from bowstring,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 From his sea-struggle tore him, that the trusty war-missile
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dead beast is a poor swimmer}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Pierced to his vitals; he proved in the currents
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Less doughty at swimming whom death had offcarried.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Soon in the waters the wonderful swimmer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was straitened most sorely with sword-pointed boar-spears,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Pressed in the battle and pulled to the cliff-edge;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The liegemen then looked on the loath-fashioned stranger.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf prepares for a struggle with the monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf donned then his battle-equipments,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cared little for life; inlaid and most ample,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hand-woven corslet which could cover his body,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Must the wave-deeps explore, that war might be powerless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To harm the great hero, and the hating one's grasp might
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not peril his safety; his head was protected
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By the light-flashing helmet that should mix with the bottoms,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Trying the eddies, treasure-emblazoned,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Encircled with jewels, as in seasons long past
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weapon-smith worked it, wondrously made it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With swine-bodies fashioned it, that thenceforward no longer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Brand might bite it, and battle-sword hurt it.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And that was not least of helpers in prowess
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He has Unferth's sword in his hand.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 That Hrothgar's spokesman had lent him when straitened;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the hilted hand-sword was Hrunting entitled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old and most excellent 'mong all of the treasures;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Its blade was of iron, blotted with poison,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hardened with gore; it failed not in battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 Any hero under heaven in hand who it brandished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who ventured to take the terrible journeys,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The battle-field sought; not the earliest occasion
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That deeds of daring 'twas destined to 'complish.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unferth has little use for swords.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ecglaf's kinsman minded not soothly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Exulting in strength, what erst he had spoken
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Drunken with wine, when the weapon he lent to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A sword-hero bolder; himself did not venture
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath the strife of the currents his life to endanger,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[51]      To fame-deeds perform; there he forfeited glory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Repute for his strength. Not so with the other
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he clad in his corslet had equipped him for battle.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF'S FIGHT WITH GRENDEL'S MOTHER.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf makes a parting speech to Hrothgar.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, Ecgtheow's son:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Recall now, oh, famous kinsman of Healfdene,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prince very prudent, now to part I am ready,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-friend of earlmen, what erst we agreed on,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{If I fail, act as a kind liegelord to my thanes,}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Should I lay down my life in lending thee assistance,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When my earth-joys were over, thou wouldst evermore serve me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In stead of a father; my faithful thanemen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My trusty retainers, protect thou and care for,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fall I in battle: and, Hrothgar belovèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and send Higelac the jewels thou hast given me}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Send unto Higelac the high-valued jewels
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou to me hast allotted. The lord of the Geatmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          May perceive from the gold, the Hrethling may see it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I should like my king to know how generous a lord I found thee to be.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he looks on the jewels, that a gem-giver found I
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Good over-measure, enjoyed him while able.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 And the ancient heirloom Unferth permit thou,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The famed one to have, the heavy-sword splendid[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hard-edgèd weapon; with Hrunting to aid me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I shall gain me glory, or grim-death shall take me."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is eager for the fray.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling of Geatmen uttered these words and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Heroic did hasten, not any rejoinder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was willing to wait for; the wave-current swallowed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He is a whole day reaching the bottom of the sea.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The doughty-in-battle. Then a day's-length elapsed ere
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was able to see the sea at its bottom.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Early she found then who fifty of winters
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The course of the currents kept in her fury,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grisly and greedy, that the grim one's dominion
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[52]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's mother knows that some one has reached her domains.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Some one of men from above was exploring.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forth did she grab them, grappled the warrior
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With horrible clutches; yet no sooner she injured
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 His body unscathèd: the burnie out-guarded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That she proved but powerless to pierce through the armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The limb-mail locked, with loath-grabbing fingers.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sea-wolf bare then, when bottomward came she,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She grabs him, and bears him to her den.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ring-prince homeward, that he after was powerless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 (He had daring to do it) to deal with his weapons,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But many a mere-beast tormented him swimming,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sea-monsters bite and strike him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Flood-beasts no few with fierce-biting tusks did
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Break through his burnie, the brave one pursued they.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earl then discovered he was down in some cavern
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Where no water whatever anywise harmed him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the clutch of the current could come not anear him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since the roofed-hall prevented; brightness a-gleaming
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fire-light he saw, flashing resplendent.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The good one saw then the sea-bottom's monster,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf attacks the mother of Grendel.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 The mighty mere-woman; he made a great onset
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With weapon-of-battle, his hand not desisted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From striking, that war-blade struck on her head then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A battle-song greedy. The stranger perceived then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The sword will not bite.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sword would not bite, her life would not injure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 But the falchion failed the folk-prince when straitened:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Erst had it often onsets encountered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oft cloven the helmet, the fated one's armor:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas the first time that ever the excellent jewel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had failed of its fame. Firm-mooded after,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Not heedless of valor, but mindful of glory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was Higelac's kinsman; the hero-chief angry
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cast then his carved-sword covered with jewels
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That it lay on the earth, hard and steel-pointed;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hero throws down all weapons, and again trusts to his hand-grip.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He hoped in his strength, his hand-grapple sturdy.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 So any must act whenever he thinketh
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To gain him in battle glory unending,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And is reckless of living. The lord of the War-Geats
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[53]      (He shrank not from battle) seized by the shoulder[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mother of Grendel; then mighty in struggle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Swung he his enemy, since his anger was kindled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That she fell to the floor. With furious grapple
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf falls.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She gave him requital[3] early thereafter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And stretched out to grab him; the strongest of warriors
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faint-mooded stumbled, till he fell in his traces,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The monster sits on him with drawn sword.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Foot-going champion. Then she sat on the hall-guest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And wielded her war-knife wide-bladed, flashing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For her son would take vengeance, her one only bairn.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His armor saves his life.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His breast-armor woven bode on his shoulder;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          It guarded his life, the entrance defended
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 'Gainst sword-point and edges. Ecgtheow's son there
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had fatally journeyed, champion of Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the arms of the ocean, had the armor not given,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Close-woven corslet, comfort and succor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God arranged for his escape.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And had God most holy not awarded the victory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 All-knowing Lord; easily did heaven's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ruler most righteous arrange it with justice;[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Uprose he erect ready for battle.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] Kl. emends 'wæl-sweord.' The half-line would then read, '_the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    battle-sword splendid_.'--For 'heard-ecg' in next half-verse, see note
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    to 20_39 above.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] Sw., R., and t.B. suggest 'feaxe' for 'eaxle' (1538) and render:

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] If 'hand-léan' be accepted (as the MS. has it), the line will

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXIV.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF IS DOUBLE-CONQUEROR.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf grasps a giant-sword,}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then he saw mid the war-gems a weapon of victory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An ancient giant-sword, of edges a-doughty,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glory of warriors: of weapons 'twas choicest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Only 'twas larger than any man else was
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[54]    5 Able to bear to the battle-encounter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The good and splendid work of the giants.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He grasped then the sword-hilt, knight of the Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bold and battle-grim, brandished his ring-sword,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hopeless of living, hotly he smote her,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 That the fiend-woman's neck firmly it grappled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and fells the female monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Broke through her bone-joints, the bill fully pierced her
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fate-cursèd body, she fell to the ground then:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hand-sword was bloody, the hero exulted.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brand was brilliant, brightly it glimmered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Just as from heaven gemlike shineth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The torch of the firmament. He glanced 'long the building,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And turned by the wall then, Higelac's vassal
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Raging and wrathful raised his battle-sword
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Strong by the handle. The edge was not useless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To the hero-in-battle, but he speedily wished to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Give Grendel requital for the many assaults he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had worked on the West-Danes not once, but often,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he slew in slumber the subjects of Hrothgar,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swallowed down fifteen sleeping retainers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Of the folk of the Danemen, and fully as many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carried away, a horrible prey.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He gave him requital, grim-raging champion,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf sees the body of Grendel, and cuts off his head.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he saw on his rest-place weary of conflict
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grendel lying, of life-joys bereavèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 As the battle at Heorot erstwhile had scathed him;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His body far bounded, a blow when he suffered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Death having seized him, sword-smiting heavy,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And he cut off his head then. Early this noticed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The clever carles who as comrades of Hrothgar
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The waters are gory.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Gazed on the sea-deeps, that the surging wave-currents
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were mightily mingled, the mere-flood was gory:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the good one the gray-haired together held converse,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is given up for dead.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoary of head, that they hoped not to see again
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling ever, that exulting in victory
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 He'd return there to visit the distinguished folk-ruler:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[55]      Then many concluded the mere-wolf had killed him.[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ninth hour came then. From the ness-edge departed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bold-mooded Scyldings; the gold-friend of heroes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Homeward betook him. The strangers sat down then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Soul-sick, sorrowful, the sea-waves regarding:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They wished and yet weened not their well-loved friend-lord
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The giant-sword melts.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To see any more. The sword-blade began then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blood having touched it, contracting and shriveling
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With battle-icicles; 'twas a wonderful marvel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 That it melted entirely, likest to ice when
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Father unbindeth the bond of the frost and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Unwindeth the wave-bands, He who wieldeth dominion
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of times and of tides: a truth-firm Creator.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor took he of jewels more in the dwelling,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Lord of the Weders, though they lay all around him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Than the head and the handle handsome with jewels;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[56]      The brand early melted, burnt was the weapon:[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So hot was the blood, the strange-spirit poisonous
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hero swims back to the realms of day.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That in it did perish. He early swam off then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Who had bided in combat the carnage of haters,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went up through the ocean; the eddies were cleansèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The spacious expanses, when the spirit from farland
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His life put aside and this short-lived existence.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The seamen's defender came swimming to land then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Doughty of spirit, rejoiced in his sea-gift,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bulky burden which he bore in his keeping.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The excellent vassals advanced then to meet him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To God they were grateful, were glad in their chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That to see him safe and sound was granted them.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 From the high-minded hero, then, helmet and burnie
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were speedily loosened: the ocean was putrid,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The water 'neath welkin weltered with gore.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forth did they fare, then, their footsteps retracing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Merry and mirthful, measured the earth-way,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 The highway familiar: men very daring[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bare then the head from the sea-cliff, burdening
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the earlmen, excellent-valiant.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{It takes four men to carry Grendel's head on a spear.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Four of them had to carry with labor
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The head of Grendel to the high towering gold-hall
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Upstuck on the spear, till fourteen most-valiant
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And battle-brave Geatmen came there going
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Straight to the palace: the prince of the people
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measured the mead-ways, their mood-brave companion.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling of earlmen entered the building,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Deed-valiant man, adorned with distinction,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Doughty shield-warrior, to address King Hrothgar:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[57]      Then hung by the hair, the head of Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was borne to the building, where beer-thanes were drinking,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Loth before earlmen and eke 'fore the lady:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       90 The warriors beheld then a wonderful sight.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Þæs monige gewearð' (1599) and 'hafað þæs geworden' (2027).--In a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    paper published some years ago in one of the Johns Hopkins University
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    circulars, I tried to throw upon these two long-doubtful passages some
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    light derived from a study of like passages in Alfred's prose.--The
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    impersonal verb 'geweorðan,' with an accus. of the person, and a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    þæt-clause is used several times with the meaning 'agree.' See Orosius
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (Sweet's ed.) 178_7; 204_34; 208_28; 210_15; 280_20. In the two
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Beowulf passages, the þæt-clause is anticipated by 'þæs,' which is
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    clearly a gen. of the thing agreed on.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The first passage (v. 1599 (b)-1600) I translate literally: _Then many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    agreed upon this (namely), that the sea-wolf had killed him_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The second passage (v. 2025 (b)-2027): _She is promised ...; to this
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the friend of the Scyldings has agreed, etc_. By emending 'is' instead
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of 'wæs' (2025), the tenses will be brought into perfect harmony.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    In v. 1997 ff. this same idiom occurs, and was noticed in B.'s great
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    article on Beowulf, which appeared about the time I published my
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reading of 1599 and 2027. Translate 1997 then: _Wouldst let the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    South-Danes themselves decide about their struggle with Grendel_. Here
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'Súð-Dene' is accus. of person, and 'gúðe' is gen. of thing agreed on.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    With such collateral support as that afforded by B. (P. and B. XII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    97), I have no hesitation in departing from H.-So., my usual guide.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The idiom above treated runs through A.-S., Old Saxon, and other
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Teutonic languages, and should be noticed in the lexicons.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] 'Bróden-mæl' is regarded by most scholars as meaning a damaskeened
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    sword. Translate: _The damaskeened sword burned up_. Cf. 25_16 and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    note.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] 'Cyning-balde' (1635) is the much-disputed reading of K. and Th.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    To render this, "_nobly bold_," "_excellently bold_," have been
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggested. B. would read 'cyning-holde' (cf. 290), and render: _Men
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    well-disposed towards the king carried the head, etc._ 'Cynebealde,'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    says t.B., endorsing Gr.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXV.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF BRINGS HIS TROPHIES.--HROTHGAR'S GRATITUDE.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf relates his last exploit.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, offspring of Ecgtheow:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Lo! we blithely have brought thee, bairn of Healfdene,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prince of the Scyldings, these presents from ocean
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which thine eye looketh on, for an emblem of glory.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 I came off alive from this, narrowly 'scaping:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In war 'neath the water the work with great pains I
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Performed, and the fight had been finished quite nearly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had God not defended me. I failed in the battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Aught to accomplish, aided by Hrunting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Though that weapon was worthy, but the Wielder of earth-folk
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God was fighting with me.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gave me willingly to see on the wall a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heavy old hand-sword hanging in splendor
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (He guided most often the lorn and the friendless),
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That I swung as a weapon. The wards of the house then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 I killed in the conflict (when occasion was given me).
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the battle-sword burned, the brand that was lifted,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As the blood-current sprang, hottest of war-sweats;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seizing the hilt, from my foes I offbore it;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I avenged as I ought to their acts of malignity,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The murder of Danemen. I then make thee this promise,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heorot is freed from monsters.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou'lt be able in Heorot careless to slumber
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With thy throng of heroes and the thanes of thy people
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Every and each, of greater and lesser,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And thou needest not fear for them from the selfsame direction
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 As thou formerly fearedst, oh, folk-lord of Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[58]     End-day for earlmen." To the age-hoary man then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The famous sword is presented to Hrothgar.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gray-haired chieftain, the gold-fashioned sword-hilt,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old-work of giants, was thereupon given;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since the fall of the fiends, it fell to the keeping
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Of the wielder of Danemen, the wonder-smith's labor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the bad-mooded being abandoned this world then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Opponent of God, victim of murder,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And also his mother; it went to the keeping
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the best of the world-kings, where waters encircle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Who the scot divided in Scylding dominion.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar looks closely at the old sword.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar discoursed, the hilt he regarded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ancient heirloom where an old-time contention's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beginning was graven: the gurgling currents,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The flood slew thereafter the race of the giants,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 They had proved themselves daring: that people was loth to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{It had belonged to a race hateful to God.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Lord everlasting, through lash of the billows
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Father gave them final requital.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So in letters of rune on the clasp of the handle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gleaming and golden, 'twas graven exactly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Set forth and said, whom that sword had been made for,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Finest of irons, who first it was wrought for,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wreathed at its handle and gleaming with serpents.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wise one then said (silent they all were)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar praises Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Son of old Healfdene: "He may say unrefuted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Who performs 'mid the folk-men fairness and truth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (The hoary old ruler remembers the past),
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That better by birth is this bairn of the nobles!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy fame is extended through far-away countries,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Good friend Beowulf, o'er all of the races,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Thou holdest all firmly, hero-like strength with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prudence of spirit. I'll prove myself grateful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As before we agreed on; thou granted for long shalt
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Become a great comfort to kinsmen and comrades,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heremod's career is again contrasted with Beowulf's.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A help unto heroes. Heremod became not
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Such to the Scyldings, successors of Ecgwela;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He grew not to please them, but grievous destruction,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[59]      And diresome death-woes to Danemen attracted;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He slew in anger his table-companions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Trustworthy counsellors, till he turned off lonely
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 From world-joys away, wide-famous ruler:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though high-ruling heaven in hero-strength raised him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In might exalted him, o'er men of all nations
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Made him supreme, yet a murderous spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grew in his bosom: he gave then no ring-gems
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A wretched failure of a king, to give no jewels to his retainers.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 To the Danes after custom; endured he unjoyful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Standing the straits from strife that was raging,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Longsome folk-sorrow. Learn then from this,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lay hold of virtue! Though laden with winters,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I have sung thee these measures. 'Tis a marvel to tell it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar moralizes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 How all-ruling God from greatness of spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Giveth wisdom to children of men,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Manor and earlship: all things He ruleth.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He often permitteth the mood-thought of man of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The illustrious lineage to lean to possessions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Allows him earthly delights at his manor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A high-burg of heroes to hold in his keeping,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Maketh portions of earth-folk hear him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And a wide-reaching kingdom so that, wisdom failing him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He himself is unable to reckon its boundaries;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 He liveth in luxury, little debars him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor sickness nor age, no treachery-sorrow
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Becloudeth his spirit, conflict nowhere,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No sword-hate, appeareth, but all of the world doth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wend as he wisheth; the worse he knoweth not,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       90 Till arrant arrogance inward pervading,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Waxeth and springeth, when the warder is sleeping,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The guard of the soul: with sorrows encompassed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Too sound is his slumber, the slayer is near him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who with bow and arrow aimeth in malice.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[60]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] Or rather, perhaps, '_the inlaid, or damaskeened weapon_.' Cf.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    24_57 and note.
