BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXVI.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR MORALIZES.--REST AFTER LABOR.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A wounded spirit.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Then bruised in his bosom he with bitter-toothed missile
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is hurt 'neath his helmet: from harmful pollution
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He is powerless to shield him by the wonderful mandates
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the loath-cursèd spirit; what too long he hath holden
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Him seemeth too small, savage he hoardeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor boastfully giveth gold-plated rings,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fate of the future flouts and forgetteth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since God had erst given him greatness no little,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wielder of Glory. His end-day anear,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 It afterward happens that the bodily-dwelling
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fleetingly fadeth, falls into ruins;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Another lays hold who doleth the ornaments,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The nobleman's jewels, nothing lamenting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heedeth no terror. Oh, Beowulf dear,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Best of the heroes, from bale-strife defend thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And choose thee the better, counsels eternal;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Be not over proud: life is fleeting, and its strength soon wasteth away.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beware of arrogance, world-famous champion!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But a little-while lasts thy life-vigor's fulness;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twill after hap early, that illness or sword-edge
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Shall part thee from strength, or the grasp of the fire,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or the wave of the current, or clutch of the edges,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or flight of the war-spear, or age with its horrors,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or thine eyes' bright flashing shall fade into darkness:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twill happen full early, excellent hero,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar gives an account of his reign.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 That death shall subdue thee. So the Danes a half-century
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I held under heaven, helped them in struggles
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst many a race in middle-earth's regions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With ash-wood and edges, that enemies none
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On earth molested me. Lo! offsetting change, now,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[61]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sorrow after joy.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Came to my manor, grief after joyance,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When Grendel became my constant visitor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Inveterate hater: I from that malice
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Continually travailed with trouble no little.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thanks be to God that I gained in my lifetime,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 To the Lord everlasting, to look on the gory
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Head with mine eyes, after long-lasting sorrow!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Go to the bench now, battle-adornèd
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Joy in the feasting: of jewels in common
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We'll meet with many when morning appeareth."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The Geatman was gladsome, ganged he immediately
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To go to the bench, as the clever one bade him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then again as before were the famous-for-prowess,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hall-inhabiters, handsomely banqueted,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Feasted anew. The night-veil fell then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Dark o'er the warriors. The courtiers rose then;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gray-haired was anxious to go to his slumbers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoary old Scylding. Hankered the Geatman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is fagged, and seeks rest.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The champion doughty, greatly, to rest him:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An earlman early outward did lead him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Fagged from his faring, from far-country springing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who for etiquette's sake all of a liegeman's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Needs regarded, such as seamen at that time
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were bounden to feel. The big-hearted rested;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building uptowered, spacious and gilded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 The guest within slumbered, till the sable-clad raven
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Blithely foreboded the beacon of heaven.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the bright-shining sun o'er the bottoms came going;[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The warriors hastened, the heads of the peoples
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were ready to go again to their peoples,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The Geats prepare to leave Dane-land.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The high-mooded farer would faraway thenceward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Look for his vessel. The valiant one bade then,[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[62]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unferth asks Beowulf to accept his sword as a gift. Beowulf thanks him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Ecglaf, off to bear Hrunting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To take his weapon, his well-beloved iron;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He him thanked for the gift, saying good he accounted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 The war-friend and mighty, nor chid he with words then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blade of the brand: 'twas a brave-mooded hero.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the warriors were ready, arrayed in their trappings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling dear to the Danemen advanced then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On to the dais, where the other was sitting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Grim-mooded hero, greeted King Hrothgar.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] K. says '_proudly giveth_.'--Gr. says, '_And gives no gold-plated
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    rings, in order to incite the recipient to boastfulness_.'--B.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggests 'gyld' for 'gylp,' and renders: _And gives no beaten rings
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    for reward_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] If S.'s emendation be accepted, v. 57 will read: _Then came the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    light, going bright after darkness: the warriors, etc_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] As the passage stands in H.-So., Unferth presents Beowulf with the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    sword Hrunting, and B. thanks him for the gift. If, however, the

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    weapon; he (B.) thanked him (U.) for the loan, etc_.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXVII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tSORROW AT PARTING.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's farewell.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, Ecgtheow's offspring:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "We men of the water wish to declare now
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fared from far-lands, we're firmly determined
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To seek King Higelac. Here have we fitly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Been welcomed and feasted, as heart would desire it;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Good was the greeting. If greater affection
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I am anywise able ever on earth to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gain at thy hands, ruler of heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Than yet I have done, I shall quickly be ready
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I shall be ever ready to aid thee.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 For combat and conflict. O'er the course of the waters
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Learn I that neighbors alarm thee with terror,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As haters did whilom, I hither will bring thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For help unto heroes henchmen by thousands.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My liegelord will encourage me in aiding thee.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I know as to Higelac, the lord of the Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Though young in years, he yet will permit me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By words and by works, ward of the people,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fully to furnish thee forces and bear thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My lance to relieve thee, if liegemen shall fail thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And help of my hand-strength; if Hrethric be treating,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[63]   20 Bairn of the king, at the court of the Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He thereat may find him friends in abundance:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faraway countries he were better to seek for
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who trusts in himself." Hrothgar discoursed then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Making rejoinder: "These words thou hast uttered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 All-knowing God hath given thy spirit!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{O Beowulf, thou art wise beyond thy years.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ne'er heard I an earlman thus early in life
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          More clever in speaking: thou'rt cautious of spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mighty of muscle, in mouth-answers prudent.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I count on the hope that, happen it ever
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 That missile shall rob thee of Hrethel's descendant,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Edge-horrid battle, and illness or weapon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Deprive thee of prince, of people's protector,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Should Higelac die, the Geats could find no better successor than thou
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\twouldst make.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And life thou yet holdest, the Sea-Geats will never
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Find a more fitting folk-lord to choose them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Gem-ward of heroes, than _thou_ mightest prove thee,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If the kingdom of kinsmen thou carest to govern.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy mood-spirit likes me the longer the better,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf dear: thou hast brought it to pass that
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To both these peoples peace shall be common,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Thou hast healed the ancient breach between our races.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 To Geat-folk and Danemen, the strife be suspended,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The secret assailings they suffered in yore-days;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And also that jewels be shared while I govern
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wide-stretching kingdom, and that many shall visit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Others o'er the ocean with excellent gift-gems:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 The ring-adorned bark shall bring o'er the currents
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Presents and love-gifts. This people I know
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tow'rd foeman and friend firmly established,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          After ancient etiquette everywise blameless."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the warden of earlmen gave him still farther,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Parting gifts}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Kinsman of Healfdene, a dozen of jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bade him safely seek with the presents
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His well-beloved people, early returning.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[64]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar kisses Beowulf, and weeps.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the noble-born king kissed the distinguished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dear-lovèd liegeman, the Dane-prince saluted him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 And claspèd his neck; tears from him fell,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From the gray-headed man: he two things expected,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Agèd and reverend, but rather the second,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [2]That bold in council they'd meet thereafter.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The man was so dear that he failed to suppress the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Emotions that moved him, but in mood-fetters fastened
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The old king is deeply grieved to part with his benefactor.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The long-famous hero longeth in secret
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Deep in his spirit for the dear-beloved man
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though not a blood-kinsman. Beowulf thenceward,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-splendid warrior, walked o'er the meadows
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Exulting in treasure: the sea-going vessel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Riding at anchor awaited its owner.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As they pressed on their way then, the present of Hrothgar
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Giving liberally is the true proof of kingship.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was frequently referred to: a folk-king indeed that
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Everyway blameless, till age did debar him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 The joys of his might, which hath many oft injured.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'geworhte,' the crux of this passage, B. proposes 'geþóhte,'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    rendering: _I know this people with firm thought every way blameless
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    towards foe and friends_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] S. and B. emend so as to negative the verb 'meet.' "Why should
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrothgar weep if he expects to meet Beowulf again?" both these
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    scholars ask. But the weeping is mentioned before the 'expectations':
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the tears may have been due to many emotions, especially gratitude,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    struggling for expression.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXVIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE HOMEWARD JOURNEY.--THE TWO QUEENS.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the band of very valiant retainers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came to the current; they were clad all in armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The coast-guard again.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In link-woven burnies. The land-warder noticed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The return of the earlmen, as he erstwhile had seen them;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Nowise with insult he greeted the strangers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From the naze of the cliff, but rode on to meet them;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Said the bright-armored visitors[1] vesselward traveled
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[65]      Welcome to Weders. The wide-bosomed craft then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lay on the sand, laden with armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 With horses and jewels, the ring-stemmèd sailer:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mast uptowered o'er the treasure of Hrothgar.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf gives the guard a handsome sword.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the boat-ward a gold-bound brand he presented,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That he was afterwards honored on the ale-bench more highly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As the heirloom's owner. [2]Set he out on his vessel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 To drive on the deep, Dane-country left he.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Along by the mast then a sea-garment fluttered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A rope-fastened sail. The sea-boat resounded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wind o'er the waters the wave-floater nowise
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Kept from its journey; the sea-goer traveled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The foamy-necked floated forth o'er the currents,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The well-fashioned vessel o'er the ways of the ocean,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The Geats see their own land again.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till they came within sight of the cliffs of the Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The well-known headlands. The wave-goer hastened
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Driven by breezes, stood on the shore.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The port-warden is anxiously looking for them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Prompt at the ocean, the port-ward was ready,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who long in the past outlooked in the distance,[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At water's-edge waiting well-lovèd heroes;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He bound to the bank then the broad-bosomed vessel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fast in its fetters, lest the force of the waters
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Should be able to injure the ocean-wood winsome.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bade he up then take the treasure of princes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Plate-gold and fretwork; not far was it thence
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To go off in search of the giver of jewels:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[66]      Hrethel's son Higelac at home there remaineth,[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Himself with his comrades close to the sea-coast.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building was splendid, the king heroic,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Great in his hall, Hygd very young was,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hygd, the noble queen of Higelac, lavish of gifts.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fine-mooded, clever, though few were the winters
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the daughter of Hæreth had dwelt in the borough;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 But she nowise was cringing nor niggard of presents,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of ornaments rare, to the race of the Geatmen.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Offa's consort, Thrytho, is contrasted with Hygd.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thrytho nursed anger, excellent[5] folk-queen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hot-burning hatred: no hero whatever
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mong household companions, her husband excepted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She is a terror to all save her husband.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Dared to adventure to look at the woman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With eyes in the daytime;[6] but he knew that death-chains
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-wreathed were wrought him: early thereafter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the hand-strife was over, edges were ready,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That fierce-raging sword-point had to force a decision,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Murder-bale show. Such no womanly custom
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For a lady to practise, though lovely her person,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That a weaver-of-peace, on pretence of anger
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A belovèd liegeman of life should deprive.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Soothly this hindered Heming's kinsman;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Other ale-drinking earlmen asserted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That fearful folk-sorrows fewer she wrought them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Treacherous doings, since first she was given
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Adorned with gold to the war-hero youthful,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For her origin honored, when Offa's great palace
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 O'er the fallow flood by her father's instructions
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She sought on her journey, where she afterwards fully,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Famed for her virtue, her fate on the king's-seat
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[67]      Enjoyed in her lifetime, love did she hold with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ruler of heroes, the best, it is told me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Of all of the earthmen that oceans encompass,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of earl-kindreds endless; hence Offa was famous
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far and widely, by gifts and by battles,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Spear-valiant hero; the home of his fathers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He governed with wisdom, whence Eomær did issue
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 For help unto heroes, Heming's kinsman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grandson of Garmund, great in encounters.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'scawan' (1896), 'scaðan' has been proposed. Accepting this,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    we may render: _He said the bright-armored warriors were going to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    their vessel, welcome, etc_. (Cf. 1804.)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] R. suggests, 'Gewát him on naca,' and renders: _The vessel set
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    out, to drive on the sea, the Dane-country left_. 'On' bears the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    alliteration; cf. 'on hafu' (2524). This has some advantages over the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    H.-So. reading; viz. (1) It adds nothing to the text; (2) it makes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'naca' the subject, and thus brings the passage into keeping with the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    context, where the poet has exhausted his vocabulary in detailing the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    actions of the vessel.--B.'s emendation (cf. P. and B. XII. 97) is
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    violent.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] B. translates: _Who for a long time, ready at the coast, had
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    looked out into the distance eagerly for the dear men_. This changes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the syntax of 'léofra manna.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] For 'wunað' (v. 1924) several eminent critics suggest 'wunade'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (=remained). This makes the passage much clearer.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] Why should such a woman be described as an 'excellent' queen? C.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggests 'frécnu' = dangerous, bold.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] For 'an dæges' various readings have been offered. If 'and-éges'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    be accepted, the sentence will read: _No hero ... dared look upon her,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    eye to eye_. If 'án-dæges' be adopted, translate: _Dared look upon her
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the whole day_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXIX.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF AND HIGELAC.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the brave one departed, his band along with him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf and his party seek Higelac.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seeking the sea-shore, the sea-marches treading,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wide-stretching shores. The world-candle glimmered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sun from the southward; they proceeded then onward,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Early arriving where they heard that the troop-lord,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ongentheow's slayer, excellent, youthful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Folk-prince and warrior was distributing jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Close in his castle. The coming of Beowulf
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was announced in a message quickly to Higelac,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 That the folk-troop's defender forth to the palace
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The linden-companion alive was advancing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Secure from the combat courtward a-going.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building was early inward made ready
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the foot-going guests as the good one had ordered.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf sits by his liegelord.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 He sat by the man then who had lived through the struggle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Kinsman by kinsman, when the king of the people
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had in lordly language saluted the dear one,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Queen Hygd receives the heroes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In words that were formal. The daughter of Hæreth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Coursed through the building, carrying mead-cups:[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[68]   20 She loved the retainers, tendered the beakers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the high-minded Geatmen. Higelac 'gan then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Higelac is greatly interested in Beowulf's adventures.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Pleasantly plying his companion with questions
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the high-towering palace. A curious interest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tormented his spirit, what meaning to see in
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The Sea-Geats' adventures: "Beowulf worthy,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Give an account of thy adventures, Beowulf dear.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How throve your journeying, when thou thoughtest suddenly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far o'er the salt-streams to seek an encounter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A battle at Heorot? Hast bettered for Hrothgar,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The famous folk-leader, his far-published sorrows
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Any at all? In agony-billows
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My suspense has been great.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I mused upon torture, distrusted the journey
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the belovèd liegeman; I long time did pray thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By no means to seek out the murderous spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To suffer the South-Danes themselves to decide on[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Grappling with Grendel. To God I am thankful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To be suffered to see thee safe from thy journey."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf narrates his adventures.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, bairn of old Ecgtheow:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "'Tis hidden by no means, Higelac chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From many of men, the meeting so famous,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 What mournful moments of me and of Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were passed in the place where he pressing affliction
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the Victory-Scyldings scathefully brought,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Anguish forever; that all I avengèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So that any under heaven of the kinsmen of Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's kindred have no cause to boast.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Needeth not boast of that cry-in-the-morning,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who longest liveth of the loth-going kindred,[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Encompassed by moorland. I came in my journey
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the royal ring-hall, Hrothgar to greet there:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar received me very cordially.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Soon did the famous scion of Healfdene,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 When he understood fully the spirit that led me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Assign me a seat with the son of his bosom.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[69]      The troop was in joyance; mead-glee greater
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath arch of the ether not ever beheld I
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The queen also showed up no little honor.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mid hall-building holders. The highly-famed queen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Peace-tie of peoples, oft passed through the building,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cheered the young troopers; she oft tendered a hero
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A beautiful ring-band, ere she went to her sitting.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar's lovely daughter.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oft the daughter of Hrothgar in view of the courtiers
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the earls at the end the ale-vessel carried,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Whom Freaware I heard then hall-sitters title,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When nail-adorned jewels she gave to the heroes:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She is betrothed to Ingeld, in order to unite the Danes and Heathobards.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-bedecked, youthful, to the glad son of Froda
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her faith has been plighted; the friend of the Scyldings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The guard of the kingdom, hath given his sanction,[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 And counts it a vantage, for a part of the quarrels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A portion of hatred, to pay with the woman.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [5]Somewhere not rarely, when the ruler has fallen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The life-taking lance relaxeth its fury
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For a brief breathing-spell, though the bride be charming!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Meodu-scencum' (1981) some would render '_with mead-pourers_.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Translate then: _The daughter of Hæreth went through the building
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    accompanied by mead-pourers_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] See my note to 1599, supra, and B. in P. and B. XII. 97.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 'fenne,' supplied by Grdtvg., B. suggests 'fácne' (cf. Jul.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    350). Accepting this, translate: _Who longest lives of the hated race,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    steeped in treachery_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] See note to v. 1599 above.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] This is perhaps the least understood sentence in the poem, almost
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    every word being open to dispute. (1) The 'nó' of our text is an
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    emendation, and is rejected by many scholars. (2) 'Seldan' is by some
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    taken as an adv. (= _seldom_), and by others as a noun (= _page_,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _companion_). (3) 'Léod-hryre,' some render '_fall of the people_';
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    others, '_fall of the prince_.' (4) 'Búgeð,' most scholars regard as
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the intrans. verb meaning '_bend_,' '_rest_'; but one great scholar has
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translated it '_shall kill_.' (5) 'Hwær,' Very recently, has been
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    attacked, 'wære' being suggested. (6) As a corollary to the above, the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    same critic proposes to drop 'oft' out of the text.--t.B. suggests: Oft
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    seldan wære after léodhryre: lýtle hwíle bongár búgeð, þéah séo brýd
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    duge = _often has a treaty been (thus) struck, after a prince had
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fallen: (but only) a short time is the spear (then) wont to rest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    however excellent the bride may be_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXX.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF NARRATES HIS ADVENTURES TO HIGELAC.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "It well may discomfit the prince of the Heathobards
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And each of the thanemen of earls that attend him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[70]      When he goes to the building escorting the woman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That a noble-born Daneman the knights should be feasting:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 There gleam on his person the leavings of elders
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hard and ring-bright, Heathobards' treasure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While they wielded their arms, till they misled to the battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their own dear lives and belovèd companions.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He saith at the banquet who the collar beholdeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 An ancient ash-warrior who earlmen's destruction
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Clearly recalleth (cruel his spirit),
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sadly beginneth sounding the youthful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thane-champion's spirit through the thoughts of his bosom,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War-grief to waken, and this word-answer speaketh:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Ingeld is stirred up to break the truce.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 'Art thou able, my friend, to know when thou seest it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brand which thy father bare to the conflict
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In his latest adventure, 'neath visor of helmet,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dearly-loved iron, where Danemen did slay him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And brave-mooded Scyldings, on the fall of the heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 (When vengeance was sleeping) the slaughter-place wielded?
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          E'en now some man of the murderer's progeny
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Exulting in ornaments enters the building,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boasts of his blood-shedding, offbeareth the jewel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which thou shouldst wholly hold in possession!'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 So he urgeth and mindeth on every occasion
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With woe-bringing words, till waxeth the season
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the woman's thane for the works of his father,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bill having bitten, blood-gory sleepeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fated to perish; the other one thenceward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 'Scapeth alive, the land knoweth thoroughly.[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the oaths of the earlmen on each side are broken,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When rancors unresting are raging in Ingeld
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And his wife-love waxeth less warm after sorrow.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So the Heathobards' favor not faithful I reckon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Their part in the treaty not true to the Danemen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their friendship not fast. I further shall tell thee
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[71]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Having made these preliminary statements, I will now tell thee of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tGrendel, the monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          More about Grendel, that thou fully mayst hear,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ornament-giver, what afterward came from
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hand-rush of heroes. When heaven's bright jewel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 O'er earthfields had glided, the stranger came raging,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The horrible night-fiend, us for to visit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where wholly unharmed the hall we were guarding.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hondscio fell first}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Hondscio happened a hopeless contention,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Death to the doomed one, dead he fell foremost,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Girded war-champion; to him Grendel became then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the vassal distinguished, a tooth-weaponed murderer,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The well-beloved henchman's body all swallowed.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not the earlier off empty of hand did
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bloody-toothed murderer, mindful of evils,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Wish to escape from the gold-giver's palace,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But sturdy of strength he strove to outdo me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-ready grappled. A glove was suspended
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Spacious and wondrous, in art-fetters fastened,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which was fashioned entirely by touch of the craftman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 From the dragon's skin by the devil's devices:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He down in its depths would do me unsadly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One among many, deed-doer raging,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though sinless he saw me; not so could it happen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When I in my anger upright did stand.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 'Tis too long to recount how requital I furnished
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For every evil to the earlmen's destroyer;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I reflected honor upon my people.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas there, my prince, that I proudly distinguished
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy land with my labors. He left and retreated,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He lived his life a little while longer:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Yet his right-hand guarded his footstep in Heorot,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And sad-mooded thence to the sea-bottom fell he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mournful in mind. For the might-rush of battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{King Hrothgar lavished gifts upon me.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The friend of the Scyldings, with gold that was plated,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With ornaments many, much requited me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 When daylight had dawned, and down to the banquet
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We had sat us together. There was chanting and joyance:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The age-stricken Scylding asked many questions
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[72]      And of old-times related; oft light-ringing harp-strings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Joy-telling wood, were touched by the brave one;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 Now he uttered measures, mourning and truthful,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the large-hearted land-king a legend of wonder
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Truthfully told us. Now troubled with years
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The age-hoary warrior afterward began to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mourn for the might that marked him in youth-days;

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Much he remembered. From morning till night then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We joyed us therein as etiquette suffered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till the second night season came unto earth-folk.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then early thereafter, the mother of Grendel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's mother.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her son had death ravished, the wrath of the Geatmen.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The horrible woman avengèd her offspring,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And with mighty mainstrength murdered a hero.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She the corpse had offcarried in the clutch of the foeman[2]

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tGIFT-GIVING IS MUTUAL.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "So the belovèd land-prince lived in decorum;

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE HOARD AND THE DRAGON.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          *       *       *       *       *       *       *
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He sought of himself who sorely did harm him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But, for need very pressing, the servant of one of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sons of the heroes hate-blows evaded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Seeking for shelter and the sin-driven warrior
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Took refuge within there. He early looked in it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          *       *       *       *       *       *       *
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          *       *       *       *       *       *       *
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[76]      *  *  *  *  *  * when the onset surprised him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hoard.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 He a gem-vessel saw there: many of suchlike
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ancient ornaments in the earth-cave were lying,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As in days of yore some one of men of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Illustrious lineage, as a legacy monstrous,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There had secreted them, careful and thoughtful,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Dear-valued jewels. Death had offsnatched them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the days of the past, and the one man moreover
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the flower of the folk who fared there the longest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was fain to defer it, friend-mourning warder,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A little longer to be left in enjoyment
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Of long-lasting treasure.[1] A barrow all-ready
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Stood on the plain the stream-currents nigh to,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          New by the ness-edge, unnethe of approaching:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The keeper of rings carried within a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [2]Ponderous deal of the treasure of nobles,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Of gold that was beaten, briefly he spake then:[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The ring-giver bewails the loss of retainers.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Hold thou, O Earth, now heroes no more may,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earnings of earlmen. Lo! erst in thy bosom
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Worthy men won them; war-death hath ravished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Perilous life-bale, all my warriors,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Liegemen belovèd, who this life have forsaken,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who hall-pleasures saw. No sword-bearer have I,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And no one to burnish the gold-plated vessel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The high-valued beaker: my heroes are vanished.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hardy helmet behung with gilding
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Shall be reaved of its riches: the ring-cleansers slumber
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who were charged to have ready visors-for-battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the burnie that bided in battle-encounter
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[77]      O'er breaking of war-shields the bite of the edges
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Moulds with the hero. The ring-twisted armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Its lord being lifeless, no longer may journey
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hanging by heroes; harp-joy is vanished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The rapture of glee-wood, no excellent falcon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swoops through the building, no swift-footed charger
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grindeth the gravel. A grievous destruction
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 No few of the world-folk widely hath scattered!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So, woful of spirit one after all
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lamented mournfully, moaning in sadness
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By day and by night, till death with its billows
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The fire-dragon}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dashed on his spirit. Then the ancient dusk-scather
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Found the great treasure standing all open,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He who flaming and fiery flies to the barrows,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Naked war-dragon, nightly escapeth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Encompassed with fire; men under heaven
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Widely beheld him. 'Tis said that he looks for[4]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 The hoard in the earth, where old he is guarding
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The heathenish treasure; he'll be nowise the better.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon meets his match.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So three-hundred winters the waster of peoples
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Held upon earth that excellent hoard-hall,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till the forementioned earlman angered him bitterly:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The beat-plated beaker he bare to his chieftain
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And fullest remission for all his remissness
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Begged of his liegelord. Then the hoard[5] was discovered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The treasure was taken, his petition was granted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hero plunders the dragon's den}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The lorn-mooded liegeman. His lord regarded
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 The old-work of earth-folk--'twas the earliest occasion.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the dragon awoke, the strife was renewed there;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He snuffed 'long the stone then, stout-hearted found he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[78]      The footprint of foeman; too far had he gone
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With cunning craftiness close to the head of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 The fire-spewing dragon. So undoomed he may 'scape from
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Anguish and exile with ease who possesseth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The favor of Heaven. The hoard-warden eagerly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Searched o'er the ground then, would meet with the person
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That caused him sorrow while in slumber reclining:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 Gleaming and wild he oft went round the cavern,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          All of it outward; not any of earthmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was seen in that desert.[6] Yet he joyed in the battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Rejoiced in the conflict: oft he turned to the barrow,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sought for the gem-cup;[7] this he soon perceived then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon perceives that some one has disturbed his treasure.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 That some man or other had discovered the gold,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The famous folk-treasure. Not fain did the hoard-ward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wait until evening; then the ward of the barrow
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was angry in spirit, the loathèd one wished to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Pay for the dear-valued drink-cup with fire.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Then the day was done as the dragon would have it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He no longer would wait on the wall, but departed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon is infuriated.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fire-impelled, flaming. Fearful the start was
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To earls in the land, as it early thereafter
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To their giver-of-gold was grievously ended.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'long-gestréona,' B. suggests 'láengestréona,' and renders,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _Of fleeting treasures_. S. accepts H.'s 'long-gestréona,' but
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    renders, _The treasure long in accumulating_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'hard-fyrdne' (2246), B. first suggested 'hard-fyndne,'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    rendering: _A heap of treasures ... so great that its equal would be
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    hard to find_. The same scholar suggests later 'hord-wynne dæl' = _A
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    deal of treasure-joy_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] Some read 'fec-word' (2247), and render: _Banning words uttered_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] An earlier reading of H.'s gave the following meaning to this
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    passage: _He is said to inhabit a mound under the earth, where he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    etc._ The translation in the text is more authentic.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] The repetition of 'hord' in this passage has led some scholars to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggest new readings to avoid the second 'hord.' This, however, is not
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    under the main stress, and, it seems to me, might easily be accepted.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] The reading of H.-So. is well defended in the notes to that
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    volume. B. emends and renders: _Nor was there any man in that desert
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    who rejoiced in conflict, in battle-work._ That is, the hoard-ward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    could not find any one who had disturbed his slumbers, for no warrior
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    was there, t.B.'s emendation would give substantially the same
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translation.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [7] 'Sinc-fæt' (2301): this word both here and in v. 2232, t.B.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    renders 'treasure.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBRAVE THOUGH AGED.--REMINISCENCES.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon spits fire.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The stranger began then to vomit forth fire,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To burn the great manor; the blaze then glimmered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For anguish to earlmen, not anything living
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[79]      Was the hateful air-goer willing to leave there.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 The war of the worm widely was noticed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The feud of the foeman afar and anear,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How the enemy injured the earls of the Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Harried with hatred: back he hied to the treasure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the well-hidden cavern ere the coming of daylight.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 He had circled with fire the folk of those regions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With brand and burning; in the barrow he trusted,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the wall and his war-might: the weening deceived him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf hears of the havoc wrought by the dragon.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then straight was the horror to Beowulf published,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Early forsooth, that his own native homestead,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 The best of buildings, was burning and melting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gift-seat of Geatmen. 'Twas a grief to the spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the good-mooded hero, the greatest of sorrows:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He fears that Heaven is punishing him for some crime.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wise one weened then that wielding his kingdom
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst the ancient commandments, he had bitterly angered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The Lord everlasting: with lorn meditations
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His bosom welled inward, as was nowise his custom.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fire-spewing dragon fully had wasted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fastness of warriors, the water-land outward,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The manor with fire. The folk-ruling hero,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Prince of the Weders, was planning to wreak him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The warmen's defender bade them to make him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earlmen's atheling, an excellent war-shield
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He orders an iron shield to be made from him, wood is useless.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wholly of iron: fully he knew then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That wood from the forest was helpless to aid him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Shield against fire. The long-worthy ruler
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Must live the last of his limited earth-days,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of life in the world and the worm along with him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though he long had been holding hoard-wealth in plenty.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He determines to fight alone.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the ring-prince disdained to seek with a war-band,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 With army extensive, the air-going ranger;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He felt no fear of the foeman's assaults and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He counted for little the might of the dragon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[80]      His power and prowess: for previously dared he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's early triumphs referred to}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A heap of hostility, hazarded dangers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 War-thane, when Hrothgar's palace he cleansèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Conquering combatant, clutched in the battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The kinsmen of Grendel, of kindred detested.[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Higelac's death recalled.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas of hand-fights not least where Higelac was slaughtered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the king of the Geatmen with clashings of battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Friend-lord of folks in Frisian dominions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Hrethrel perished through sword-drink,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With battle-swords beaten; thence Beowulf came then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On self-help relying, swam through the waters;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He bare on his arm, lone-going, thirty
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Outfits of armor, when the ocean he mounted.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Hetwars by no means had need to be boastful
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of their fighting afoot, who forward to meet him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carried their war-shields: not many returned from
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brave-mooded battle-knight back to their homesteads.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Ecgtheow's bairn o'er the bight-courses swam then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lone-goer lorn to his land-folk returning,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where Hygd to him tendered treasure and kingdom,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heardred's lack of capacity to rule.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Rings and dominion: her son she not trusted,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To be able to keep the kingdom devised him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 'Gainst alien races, on the death of King Higelac.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's tact and delicacy recalled.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yet the sad ones succeeded not in persuading the atheling
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In any way ever, to act as a suzerain
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Heardred, or promise to govern the kingdom;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yet with friendly counsel in the folk he sustained him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Gracious, with honor, till he grew to be older,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Reference is here made to a visit which Beowulf receives from Eanmund and
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tEadgils, why they come is not known.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wielded the Weders. Wide-fleeing outlaws,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ohthere's sons, sought him o'er the waters:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They had stirred a revolt 'gainst the helm of the Scylfings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The best of the sea-kings, who in Swedish dominions
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Distributed treasure, distinguished folk-leader.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[81]      'Twas the end of his earth-days; injury fatal[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By swing of the sword he received as a greeting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Higelac; Ongentheow's bairn
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Later departed to visit his homestead,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 When Heardred was dead; let Beowulf rule them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Govern the Geatmen: good was that folk-king.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Hám' (2326), the suggestion of B. is accepted by t.B. and other
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    scholars.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'láðan cynnes' (2355), t.B. suggests 'láðan cynne,' apposition
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    to 'mægum.' From syntactical and other considerations, this is a most
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    excellent emendation.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] Gr. read 'on feorme' (2386), rendering: _He there at the banquet a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fatal wound received by blows of the sword._
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXIV.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF SEEKS THE DRAGON.--BEOWULF'S REMINISCENCES.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He planned requital for the folk-leader's ruin
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In days thereafter, to Eadgils the wretched
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Becoming an enemy. Ohthere's son then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went with a war-troop o'er the wide-stretching currents
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 With warriors and weapons: with woe-journeys cold he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          After avenged him, the king's life he took.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf has been preserved through many perils.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So he came off uninjured from all of his battles,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Perilous fights, offspring of Ecgtheow,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From his deeds of daring, till that day most momentous
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 When he fate-driven fared to fight with the dragon.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{With eleven comrades, he seeks the dragon.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With eleven companions the prince of the Geatmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went lowering with fury to look at the fire-drake:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Inquiring he'd found how the feud had arisen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hate to his heroes; the highly-famed gem-vessel
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Was brought to his keeping through the hand of th' informer.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A guide leads the way, but}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That in the throng was thirteenth of heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That caused the beginning of conflict so bitter,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Captive and wretched, must sad-mooded thenceward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{very reluctantly.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Point out the place: he passed then unwillingly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To the spot where he knew of the notable cavern,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cave under earth, not far from the ocean,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The anger of eddies, which inward was full of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Jewels and wires: a warden uncanny,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[82]      Warrior weaponed, wardered the treasure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Old under earth; no easy possession
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For any of earth-folk access to get to.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the battle-brave atheling sat on the naze-edge,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While the gold-friend of Geatmen gracious saluted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His fireside-companions: woe was his spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Death-boding, wav'ring; Weird very near him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who must seize the old hero, his soul-treasure look for,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dragging aloof his life from his body:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not flesh-hidden long was the folk-leader's spirit.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, Ecgtheow's son:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's retrospect.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 "I survived in my youth-days many a conflict,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hours of onset: that all I remember.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I was seven-winters old when the jewel-prince took me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          High-lord of heroes, at the hands of my father,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrethel the hero-king had me in keeping,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrethel took me when I was seven.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Gave me treasure and feasting, our kinship remembered;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not ever was I _any_ less dear to him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He treated me as a son.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Knight in the boroughs, than the bairns of his household,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Herebald and Hæthcyn and Higelac mine.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the eldest unjustly by acts of a kinsman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Was murder-bed strewn, since him Hæthcyn from horn-bow
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{One of the brothers accidentally kills another.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His sheltering chieftain shot with an arrow,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Erred in his aim and injured his kinsman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One brother the other, with blood-sprinkled spear:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{No fee could compound for such a calamity.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas a feeless fight, finished in malice,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Sad to his spirit; the folk-prince however
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had to part from existence with vengeance untaken.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{[A parallel case is supposed.]}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So to hoar-headed hero 'tis heavily crushing[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[83]      To live to see his son as he rideth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Young on the gallows: then measures he chanteth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 A song of sorrow, when his son is hanging
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the raven's delight, and aged and hoary
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He is unable to offer any assistance.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Every morning his offspring's departure
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is constant recalled: he cares not to wait for
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The birth of an heir in his borough-enclosures,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since that one through death-pain the deeds hath experienced.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He heart-grieved beholds in the house of his son the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wine-building wasted, the wind-lodging places
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Reaved of their roaring; the riders are sleeping,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 The knights in the grave; there's no sound of the harp-wood,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Joy in the yards, as of yore were familiar.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Gomelum ceorle' (2445).--H. takes these words as referring to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrethel; but the translator here departs from his editor by
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    understanding the poet to refer to a hypothetical old man, introduced
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as an illustration of a father's sorrow.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrethrel had certainly never seen a son of his ride on the gallows to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    feed the crows.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The passage beginning 'swá bið géomorlic' seems to be an effort to
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reach a full simile, 'as ... so.' 'As it is mournful for an old man,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    etc. ... so the defence of the Weders (2463) bore heart-sorrow, etc.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The verses 2451 to 2463-1/2 would be parenthetical, the poet's feelings
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    being so strong as to interrupt the simile. The punctuation of the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fourth edition would be better--a comma after 'galgan' (2447). The
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translation may be indicated as follows: _(Just) as it is sad for an
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    old man to see his son ride young on the gallows when he himself is
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    uttering mournful measures, a sorrowful song, while his son hangs for a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    comfort to the raven, and he, old and infirm, cannot render him any
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    kelp--(he is constantly reminded, etc., 2451-2463)--so the defence of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the Weders, etc._
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
