BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXV.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tREMINISCENCES (_continued_).--BEOWULF'S LAST BATTLE.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "He seeks then his chamber, singeth a woe-song
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One for the other; all too extensive
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seemed homesteads and plains. So the helm of the Weders
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrethel grieves for Herebald.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mindful of Herebald heart-sorrow carried,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Stirred with emotion, nowise was able
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To wreak his ruin on the ruthless destroyer:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was unable to follow the warrior with hatred,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With deeds that were direful, though dear he not held him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[84]      Then pressed by the pang this pain occasioned him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 He gave up glee, God-light elected;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He left to his sons, as the man that is rich does,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His land and fortress, when from life he departed.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Strife between Swedes and Geats.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then was crime and hostility 'twixt Swedes and Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er wide-stretching water warring was mutual,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Burdensome hatred, when Hrethel had perished,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And Ongentheow's offspring were active and valiant,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wished not to hold to peace oversea, but
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Round Hreosna-beorh often accomplished
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cruelest massacre. This my kinsman avengèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The feud and fury, as 'tis found on inquiry,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though one of them paid it with forfeit of life-joys,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hæthcyn's fall at Ravenswood.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With price that was hard: the struggle became then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fatal to Hæthcyn, lord of the Geatmen.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I heard that at morning one brother the other
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 With edges of irons egged on to murder,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where Ongentheow maketh onset on Eofor:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The helmet crashed, the hoary-haired Scylfing
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sword-smitten fell, his hand then remembered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Feud-hate sufficient, refused not the death-blow.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I requited him for the jewels he gave me.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The gems that he gave me, with jewel-bright sword I
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Quited in contest, as occasion was offered:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Land he allowed me, life-joy at homestead,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Manor to live on. Little he needed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From Gepids or Danes or in Sweden to look for
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Trooper less true, with treasure to buy him;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mong foot-soldiers ever in front I would hie me,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Alone in the vanguard, and evermore gladly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Warfare shall wage, while this weapon endureth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That late and early often did serve me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf refers to his having slain Dæghrefn.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 When I proved before heroes the slayer of Dæghrefn,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Knight of the Hugmen: he by no means was suffered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the king of the Frisians to carry the jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The breast-decoration; but the banner-possessor
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bowed in the battle, brave-mooded atheling.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[85]   45 No weapon was slayer, but war-grapple broke then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The surge of his spirit, his body destroying.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Now shall weapon's edge make war for the treasure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And hand and firm-sword." Beowulf spake then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boast-words uttered--the latest occasion:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He boasts of his youthful prowess, and declares himself still fearless.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 "I braved in my youth-days battles unnumbered;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Still am I willing the struggle to look for,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fame-deeds perform, folk-warden prudent,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If the hateful despoiler forth from his cavern
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seeketh me out!" Each of the heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Helm-bearers sturdy, he thereupon greeted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His last salutations.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Belovèd co-liegemen--his last salutation:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "No brand would I bear, no blade for the dragon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wist I a way my word-boast to 'complish[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Else with the monster, as with Grendel I did it;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 But fire in the battle hot I expect there,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Furious flame-burning: so I fixed on my body
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Target and war-mail. The ward of the barrow[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I'll not flee from a foot-length, the foeman uncanny.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At the wall 'twill befall us as Fate decreeth,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Let Fate decide between us.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Each one's Creator. I am eager in spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With the wingèd war-hero to away with all boasting.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bide on the barrow with burnies protected,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wait ye here till the battle is over.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earls in armor, which of _us_ two may better
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bear his disaster, when the battle is over.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 'Tis no matter of yours, and man cannot do it,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But me and me only, to measure his strength with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The monster of malice, might-deeds to 'complish.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I with prowess shall gain the gold, or the battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[86]      Direful death-woe will drag off your ruler!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 The mighty champion rose by his shield then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Brave under helmet, in battle-mail went he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath steep-rising stone-cliffs, the strength he relied on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of one man alone: no work for a coward.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then he saw by the wall who a great many battles
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Had lived through, most worthy, when foot-troops collided,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The place of strife is described.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Stone-arches standing, stout-hearted champion,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Saw a brook from the barrow bubbling out thenceward:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The flood of the fountain was fuming with war-flame:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not nigh to the hoard, for season the briefest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Could he brave, without burning, the abyss that was yawning,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The drake was so fiery. The prince of the Weders
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Caused then that words came from his bosom,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So fierce was his fury; the firm-hearted shouted:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His battle-clear voice came in resounding
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       90 'Neath the gray-colored stone. Stirred was his hatred,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf calls out under the stone arches.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoard-ward distinguished the speech of a man;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Time was no longer to look out for friendship.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The breath of the monster issued forth first,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Vapory war-sweat, out of the stone-cave:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The terrible encounter.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       95 The earth re-echoed. The earl 'neath the barrow
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lifted his shield, lord of the Geatmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tow'rd the terrible stranger: the ring-twisted creature's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heart was then ready to seek for a struggle.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf brandishes his sword,}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and stands against his shield.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The lord of the troopers intrepidly stood then

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon coils himself.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Quickly together: in corslet he bided.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[87]  105 He went then in blazes, bended and striding,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hasting him forward. His life and body
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The targe well protected, for time-period shorter
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Than wish demanded for the well-renowned leader,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where he then for the first day was forced to be victor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t      110 Famous in battle, as Fate had not willed it.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The lord of the Geatmen uplifted his hand then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Smiting the fire-drake with sword that was precious,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That bright on the bone the blade-edge did weaken,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bit more feebly than his folk-leader needed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t      115 Burdened with bale-griefs. Then the barrow-protector,

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon rages}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the sword-blow had fallen, was fierce in his spirit,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Flinging his fires, flamings of battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gleamed then afar: the gold-friend of Weders
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's sword fails him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boasted no conquests, his battle-sword failed him

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Met with each other. Anew and afresh

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The great hero is reduced to extremities.}

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ruffled by care: kin-love can never

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXVI.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tWIGLAF THE TRUSTY.--BEOWULF IS DESERTED BY FRIENDS AND BY SWORD.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf remains true--the ideal Teutonic liegeman.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of Weohstan was Wiglaf entitled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shield-warrior precious, prince of the Scylfings,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ælfhere's kinsman: he saw his dear liegelord
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Enduring the heat 'neath helmet and visor.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Then he minded the holding that erst he had given him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf recalls Beowulf's generosity.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Wægmunding warriors' wealth-blessèd homestead,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the folk-rights his father had wielded;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was hot for the battle, his hand seized the target,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The yellow-bark shield, he unsheathed his old weapon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Which was known among earthmen as the relic of Eanmund,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ohthere's offspring, whom, exiled and friendless,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weohstan did slay with sword-edge in battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And carried his kinsman the clear-shining helmet,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ring-made burnie, the old giant-weapon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 That Onela gave him, his boon-fellow's armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ready war-trappings: he the feud did not mention,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though he'd fatally smitten the son of his brother.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many a half-year held he the treasures,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bill and the burnie, till his bairn became able,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Like his father before him, fame-deeds to 'complish;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then he gave him 'mong Geatmen a goodly array of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weeds for his warfare; he went from life then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old on his journey. 'Twas the earliest time then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{This is Wiglaf's first battle as liegeman of Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the youthful champion might charge in the battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Aiding his liegelord; his spirit was dauntless.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor did kinsman's bequest quail at the battle:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          This the dragon discovered on their coming together.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wiglaf uttered many a right-saying,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Said to his fellows, sad was his spirit:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf appeals to the pride of the cowards.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 "I remember the time when, tasting the mead-cup,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We promised in the hall the lord of us all
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[89]      Who gave us these ring-treasures, that this battle-equipment,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swords and helmets, we'd certainly quite him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Should need of such aid ever befall him:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{How we have forfeited our liegelord's confidence!}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 In the war-band he chose us for this journey spontaneously,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Stirred us to glory and gave me these jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since he held and esteemed us trust-worthy spearmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hardy helm-bearers, though this hero-achievement
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Our lord intended alone to accomplish,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Ward of his people, for most of achievements,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Doings audacious, he did among earth-folk.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Our lord is in sore need of us.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The day is now come when the ruler of earthmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Needeth the vigor of valiant heroes:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Let us wend us towards him, the war-prince to succor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 While the heat yet rageth, horrible fire-fight.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I would rather die than go home with out my suzerain.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          God wot in me, 'tis mickle the liefer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blaze should embrace my body and eat it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With my treasure-bestower. Meseemeth not proper
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To bear our battle-shields back to our country,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 'Less first we are able to fell and destroy the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Long-hating foeman, to defend the life of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Surely he does not deserve to die alone.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The prince of the Weders. Well do I know 'tisn't
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earned by his exploits, he only of Geatmen
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sorrow should suffer, sink in the battle:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Brand and helmet to us both shall be common,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [1]Shield-cover, burnie." Through the bale-smoke he stalked then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went under helmet to the help of his chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf reminds Beowulf of his youthful boasts.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Briefly discoursing: "Beowulf dear,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Perform thou all fully, as thou formerly saidst,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 In thy youthful years, that while yet thou livedst
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[90]      Thou wouldst let thine honor not ever be lessened.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy life thou shalt save, mighty in actions,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Atheling undaunted, with all of thy vigor;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The monster advances on them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I'll give thee assistance." The dragon came raging,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Wild-mooded stranger, when these words had been uttered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          ('Twas the second occasion), seeking his enemies,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Men that were hated, with hot-gleaming fire-waves;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With blaze-billows burned the board to its edges:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fight-armor failed then to furnish assistance
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 To the youthful spear-hero: but the young-agèd stripling
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Quickly advanced 'neath his kinsman's war-target,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since his own had been ground in the grip of the fire.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf strikes at the dragon.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the warrior-king was careful of glory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He soundly smote with sword-for-the-battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 That it stood in the head by hatred driven;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nægling was shivered, the old and iron-made
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His sword fails him.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Brand of Beowulf in battle deceived him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas denied him that edges of irons were able
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To help in the battle; the hand was too mighty
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 [2]Which every weapon, as I heard on inquiry,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Outstruck in its stroke, when to struggle he carried
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wonderful war-sword: it waxed him no better.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon advances on Beowulf again.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the people-despoiler--third of his onsets--
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fierce-raging fire-drake, of feud-hate was mindful,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Charged on the strong one, when chance was afforded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heated and war-grim, seized on his neck
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With teeth that were bitter; he bloody did wax with
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Soul-gore seething; sword-blood in waves boiled.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] The passage '_Brand ... burnie_,' is much disputed. In the first
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    place, some eminent critics assume a gap of at least two
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    half-verses.--'Úrum' (2660), being a peculiar form, has been much
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    discussed. 'Byrdu-scrúd' is also a crux. B. suggests 'býwdu-scrúd' =
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _splendid vestments_. Nor is 'bám' accepted by all, 'béon' being
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggested. Whatever the individual words, the passage must mean, "_I
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    intend to share with him my equipments of defence_."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] B. would render: _Which, as I heard, excelled in stroke every
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    sword that he carried to the strife, even the strongest (sword)._ For
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'Þonne' he reads 'Þone,' rel. pr.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXVII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE FATAL STRUGGLE.--BEOWULF'S LAST MOMENTS.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf defends Beowulf.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I heard that at need of the king of the people
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The upstanding earlman exhibited prowess,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Vigor and courage, as suited his nature;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [1]He his head did not guard, but the high-minded liegeman's
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Hand was consumed, when he succored his kinsman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So he struck the strife-bringing strange-comer lower,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earl-thane in armor, that _in_ went the weapon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gleaming and plated, that 'gan then the fire[2]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf draws his knife,}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Later to lessen. The liegelord himself then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Retained his consciousness, brandished his war-knife,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Battle-sharp, bitter, that he bare on his armor:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and cuts the dragon.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Weder-lord cut the worm in the middle.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They had felled the enemy (life drove out then[3]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Puissant prowess), the pair had destroyed him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Land-chiefs related: so a liegeman should prove him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A thaneman when needed. To the prince 'twas the last of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His era of conquest by his own great achievements,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[92]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's wound swells and burns.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The latest of world-deeds. The wound then began
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which the earth-dwelling dragon erstwhile had wrought him
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To burn and to swell. He soon then discovered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That bitterest bale-woe in his bosom was raging,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Poison within. The atheling advanced then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He sits down exhausted.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That along by the wall, he prudent of spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Might sit on a settle; he saw the giant-work,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 How arches of stone strengthened with pillars
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earth-hall eternal inward supported.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the long-worthy liegeman laved with his hand the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf bathes his lord's head.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far-famous chieftain, gory from sword-edge,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Refreshing the face of his friend-lord and ruler,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Sated with battle, unbinding his helmet.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, of his injury spake he,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His wound that was fatal (he was fully aware
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He had lived his allotted life-days enjoying
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The pleasures of earth; then past was entirely
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 His measure of days, death very near):
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf regrets that he has no son.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "My son I would give now my battle-equipments,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had any of heirs been after me granted,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Along of my body. This people I governed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fifty of winters: no king 'mong my neighbors
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Dared to encounter me with comrades-in-battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Try me with terror. The time to me ordered
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I bided at home, mine own kept fitly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sought me no snares, swore me not many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I can rejoice in a well-spent life.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oaths in injustice. Joy over all this
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 I'm able to have, though ill with my death-wounds;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hence the Ruler of Earthmen need not charge me
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With the killing of kinsmen, when cometh my life out
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forth from my body. Fare thou with haste now
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Bring me the hoard, Wiglaf, that my dying eyes may be refreshed by a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tsight of it.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To behold the hoard 'neath the hoar-grayish stone,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Well-lovèd Wiglaf, now the worm is a-lying,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sore-wounded sleepeth, disseized of his treasure.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Go thou in haste that treasures of old I,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-wealth may gaze on, together see lying
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[93]      The ether-bright jewels, be easier able,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Having the heap of hoard-gems, to yield my
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Life and the land-folk whom long I have governed."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] B. renders: _He_ (_W_.) did not regard his (_the dragon's_) _head_
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (since Beowulf had struck it without effect), _but struck the dragon a
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    little lower down.--_One crux is to find out _whose head_ is meant;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    another is to bring out the antithesis between 'head' and 'hand.'
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] 'Þæt þæt fýr' (2702), S. emends to 'þá þæt fýr' = _when the fire
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    began to grow less intense afterward_. This emendation relieves the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    passage of a plethora of conjunctive _þæt_'s.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 'gefyldan' (2707), S. proposes 'gefylde.' The passage would
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    read: _He felled the foe (life drove out strength), and they then both
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    had destroyed him, chieftains related_. This gives Beowulf the credit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of having felled the dragon; then they combine to annihilate him.--For
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'ellen' (2707), Kl. suggests 'e(a)llne.'--The reading '_life drove out
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    strength_' is very unsatisfactory and very peculiar. I would suggest
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as follows: Adopt S.'s emendation, remove H.'s parenthesis, read
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'ferh-ellen wræc,' and translate: _He felled the foe, drove out his
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    life-strength_ (that is, made him _hors de combat_), _and then they
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    both, etc_.

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXVIII.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tWIGLAF PLUNDERS THE DRAGON'S DEN.--BEOWULF'S DEATH.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf fulfils his lord's behest.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then heard I that Wihstan's son very quickly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          These words being uttered, heeded his liegelord
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wounded and war-sick, went in his armor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His well-woven ring-mail, 'neath the roof of the barrow.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Then the trusty retainer treasure-gems many
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon's den.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Victorious saw, when the seat he came near to,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-treasure sparkling spread on the bottom,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wonder on the wall, and the worm-creature's cavern,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ancient dawn-flier's, vessels a-standing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Cups of the ancients of cleansers bereavèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Robbed of their ornaments: there were helmets in numbers,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old and rust-eaten, arm-bracelets many,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Artfully woven. Wealth can easily,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold on the sea-bottom, turn into vanity[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Each one of earthmen, arm him who pleaseth!
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And he saw there lying an all-golden banner
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          High o'er the hoard, of hand-wonders greatest,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Linkèd with lacets: a light from it sparkled,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the floor of the cavern he was able to look on,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon is not there.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To examine the jewels. Sight of the dragon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[94]      Not any was offered, but edge offcarried him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf bears the hoard away.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I heard that the hero the hoard-treasure plundered,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The giant-work ancient reaved in the cavern,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bare on his bosom the beakers and platters,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 As himself would fain have it, and took off the standard,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brightest of beacons;[2] the bill had erst injured
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (Its edge was of iron), the old-ruler's weapon,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Him who long had watched as ward of the jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who fire-terror carried hot for the treasure,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Rolling in battle, in middlemost darkness,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till murdered he perished. The messenger hastened,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not loth to return, hurried by jewels:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Curiosity urged him if, excellent-mooded,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Alive he should find the lord of the Weders
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Mortally wounded, at the place where he left him.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mid the jewels he found then the famous old chieftain,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His liegelord belovèd, at his life's-end gory:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He thereupon 'gan to lave him with water,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till the point of his word piercèd his breast-hoard.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Beowulf spake (the gold-gems he noticed),
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is rejoiced to see the jewels.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The old one in sorrow: "For the jewels I look on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thanks do I utter for all to the Ruler,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wielder of Worship, with words of devotion,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Lord everlasting, that He let me such treasures
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Gain for my people ere death overtook me.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since I've bartered the agèd life to me granted
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For treasure of jewels, attend ye henceforward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He desires to be held in memory by his people.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wants of the war-thanes; I can wait here no longer.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The battle-famed bid ye to build them a grave-hill,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Bright when I'm burned, at the brim-current's limit;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As a memory-mark to the men I have governed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[95]      Aloft it shall tower on Whale's-Ness uprising,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That earls of the ocean hereafter may call it
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf's barrow, those who barks ever-dashing
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 From a distance shall drive o'er the darkness of waters."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hero's last gift}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bold-mooded troop-lord took from his neck then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ring that was golden, gave to his liegeman,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The youthful war-hero, his gold-flashing helmet,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His collar and war-mail, bade him well to enjoy them:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and last words.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 "Thou art latest left of the line of our kindred,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of Wægmunding people: Weird hath offcarried
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          All of my kinsmen to the Creator's glory,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earls in their vigor: I shall after them fare."
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas the aged liegelord's last-spoken word in
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 His musings of spirit, ere he mounted the fire,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The battle-waves burning: from his bosom departed
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His soul to seek the sainted ones' glory.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] The word 'oferhígian' (2767) being vague and little understood,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    two quite distinct translations of this passage have arisen. One takes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'oferhígian' as meaning 'to exceed,' and, inserting 'hord' after
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'gehwone,' renders: _The treasure may easily, the gold in the ground,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    exceed in value every hoard of man, hide it who will._ The other takes
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'oferhígian' as meaning 'to render arrogant,' and, giving the sentence
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    a moralizing tone, renders substantially as in the body of this work.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (Cf. 28_13 et seq.)
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] The passage beginning here is very much disputed. 'The bill of the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    old lord' is by some regarded as Beowulf's sword; by others, as that
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of the ancient possessor of the hoard. 'Ær gescód' (2778), translated
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    in this work as verb and adverb, is by some regarded as a compound
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    participial adj. = _sheathed in brass_.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXIX.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE DEAD FOES.--WIGLAF'S BITTER TAUNTS.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf is sorely grieved to see his lord look so un-warlike.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          It had wofully chanced then the youthful retainer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To behold on earth the most ardent-belovèd
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At his life-days' limit, lying there helpless.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The slayer too lay there, of life all bereavèd,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Horrible earth-drake, harassed with sorrow:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon has plundered his last hoard.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The round-twisted monster was permitted no longer
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To govern the ring-hoards, but edges of war-swords
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mightily seized him, battle-sharp, sturdy
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Leavings of hammers, that still from his wounds
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 The flier-from-farland fell to the earth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hard by his hoard-house, hopped he at midnight
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not e'er through the air, nor exulting in jewels
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Suffered them to see him: but he sank then to earthward
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Through the hero-chief's handwork. I heard sure it throve then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[96]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Few warriors dared to face the monster.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 But few in the land of liegemen of valor,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though of every achievement bold he had proved him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To run 'gainst the breath of the venomous scather,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or the hall of the treasure to trouble with hand-blows,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If he watching had found the ward of the hoard-hall
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 On the barrow abiding. Beowulf's part of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The treasure of jewels was paid for with death;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the twain had attained to the end of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Life so unlasting. Not long was the time till
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The cowardly thanes come out of the thicket.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The tardy-at-battle returned from the thicket,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The timid truce-breakers ten all together,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who durst not before play with the lances
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the prince of the people's pressing emergency;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They are ashamed of their desertion.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But blushing with shame, with shields they betook them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With arms and armor where the old one was lying:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 They gazed upon Wiglaf. He was sitting exhausted,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foot-going fighter, not far from the shoulders
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the lord of the people, would rouse him with water;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No whit did it help him; though he hoped for it keenly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was able on earth not at all in the leader
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Life to retain, and nowise to alter
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The will of the Wielder; the World-Ruler's power[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Would govern the actions of each one of heroes,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf is ready to excoriate them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As yet He is doing. From the young one forthwith then
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Could grim-worded greeting be got for him quickly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Whose courage had failed him. Wiglaf discoursed then,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weohstan his son, sad-mooded hero,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He begins to taunt them.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Looked on the hated: "He who soothness will utter
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Can say that the liegelord who gave you the jewels,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ornament-armor wherein ye are standing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 When on ale-bench often he offered to hall-men
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Helmet and burnie, the prince to his liegemen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As best upon earth he was able to find him,--
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[97]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Surely our lord wasted his armor on poltroons.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That he wildly wasted his war-gear undoubtedly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When battle o'ertook him.[2] The troop-king no need had
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 To glory in comrades; yet God permitted him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He, however, got along without you}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Victory-Wielder, with weapon unaided
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Himself to avenge, when vigor was needed.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I life-protection but little was able
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To give him in battle, and I 'gan, notwithstanding,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{With some aid, I could have saved our liegelord}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Helping my kinsman (my strength overtaxing):
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He waxed the weaker when with weapon I smote on
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My mortal opponent, the fire less strongly
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Flamed from his bosom. Too few of protectors
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came round the king at the critical moment.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Gift-giving is over with your people: the ring-lord is dead.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Now must ornament-taking and weapon-bestowing,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Home-joyance all, cease for your kindred,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Food for the people; each of your warriors
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Must needs be bereavèd of rights that he holdeth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In landed possessions, when faraway nobles
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Shall learn of your leaving your lord so basely,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{What is life without honor?}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dastardly deed. Death is more pleasant
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To every earlman than infamous life is!"
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'dædum rædan' (2859) B. suggests 'déað árædan,' and renders:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _The might (or judgment) of God would determine death for every man,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as he still does._
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] Some critics, H. himself in earlier editions, put the clause,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'When ... him' (A.-S. 'þá ... beget') with the following sentence;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    that is, they make it dependent upon 'þorfte' (2875) instead of upon
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'forwurpe' (2873).
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXL.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE MESSENGER OF DEATH.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf sends the news of Beowulf's death to liegemen near by.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then he charged that the battle be announced at the hedge
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Up o'er the cliff-edge, where the earl-troopers bided
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The whole of the morning, mood-wretched sat them,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bearers of battle-shields, both things expecting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 The end of his lifetime and the coming again of
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The liegelord belovèd. Little reserved he
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of news that was known, who the ness-cliff did travel,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But he truly discoursed to all that could hear him:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[98]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The messenger speaks.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Now the free-giving friend-lord of the folk of the Weders,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 The folk-prince of Geatmen, is fast in his death-bed,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By the deeds of the dragon in death-bed abideth;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Along with him lieth his life-taking foeman
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Slain with knife-wounds: he was wholly unable
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To injure at all the ill-planning monster
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf sits by our dead lord.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 With bite of his sword-edge. Wiglaf is sitting,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Wihstan, up over Beowulf,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earl o'er another whose end-day hath reached him,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Head-watch holdeth o'er heroes unliving,[1]
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Our lord's death will lead to attacks from our old foes.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For friend and for foeman. The folk now expecteth
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 A season of strife when the death of the folk-king
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Frankmen and Frisians in far-lands is published.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-hatred waxed warm 'gainst the Hugmen,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Higelac's death recalled.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When Higelac came with an army of vessels
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faring to Friesland, where the Frankmen in battle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Humbled him and bravely with overmight 'complished
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the mail-clad warrior must sink in the battle,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fell 'mid his folk-troop: no fret-gems presented
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling to earlmen; aye was denied us
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Merewing's mercy. The men of the Swedelands
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 For truce or for truth trust I but little;
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But widely 'twas known that near Ravenswood Ongentheow
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hæthcyn's fall referred to.}
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sundered Hæthcyn the Hrethling from life-joys,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When for pride overweening the War-Scylfings first did
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seek the Geatmen with savage intentions.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Early did Ohthere's age-laden father,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old and terrible, give blow in requital,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Killing the sea-king, the queen-mother rescued,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The old one his consort deprived of her gold,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Onela's mother and Ohthere's also,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[99]   40 And then followed the feud-nursing foemen till hardly,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Reaved of their ruler, they Ravenswood entered.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then with vast-numbered forces he assaulted the remnant,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weary with wounds, woe often promised
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The livelong night to the sad-hearted war-troop:
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Said he at morning would kill them with edges of weapons,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Some on the gallows for glee to the fowls.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Aid came after to the anxious-in-spirit
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At dawn of the day, after Higelac's bugle
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And trumpet-sound heard they, when the good one proceeded
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 And faring followed the flower of the troopers.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Hige-méðum' (2910) is glossed by H. as dat. plu. (= for the
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    dead). S. proposes 'hige-méðe,' nom. sing. limiting Wigláf; i.e. _W.,
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    mood-weary, holds head-watch o'er friend and foe_.--B. suggests taking
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the word as dat. inst. plu. of an abstract noun in -'u.' The
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translation would be substantially the same as S.'s.
BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
